Focus of Japanese Naval Budget: Strengthening Air Power; Responding to the Soviet Union and Controlling China 38

Tokyo. The distribution plan for the Japanese military's next year's budget has been completed. At the reception for representatives of various factions of the House of Representatives, Osumi will explain it in detail. The important focus is on responding to the Red Army in the Far East and controlling China's land and air. The total budget amounts to over 551,185,600 yen, of which over 236,886,600 yen is for regular expenses and over 314,497,000 yen is for temporary expenses. There is an increase of over 22 million yen in the total budget amount. Regarding the most important strengthening of air power, an additional budget for aviation equipment, amounting to over 8.4 million yen, has been added to the temporary expenses. By the time the Soviet Union completes its Second Five-Year Plan in 1937, preparations must be made for 39 aviation squadrons. The regular expenses include the maintenance costs of all existing aircraft, pilots, cartography, etc., totaling over 24 million yen. Adding the fixed expenditure of 88 million yen for naval aviation, the total amounts to over 110 million yen.

In addition, the conversion of aircraft carriers and heavy cruisers is also a clear indication of the Japanese Navy's special attention to strengthening air power. (Hualian News Agency dispatch from the 25th)

Tokyo. Therefore, the offensive weapons of its navy have also increased fourfold, and its defensive weapons have increased tenfold. Japanese Government Countermeasures to Parliament: Watching Opposition Party Trends; Talk of Dissolving the Diet Gaining Traction 43

Tokyo: Yesterday, Prime Minister Okada and cabinet members with seats in both houses convened to discuss countermeasures for the Diet. Minister of Commerce Machida initially advocated for dissolution. However, most cabinet members, seeing dissolution as unavoidable, proposed temporarily observing the internal situation of the Seiyukai party before making a final decision. Within the Seiyukai, the hardliners, centered around President Suzuki, advocated for submitting a comprehensive vote of no confidence. Conversely, the Kokutai Meicho-ha faction, led by Kuhara, plotted to avoid dissolution by submitting individual votes of no confidence. The centrist Nichisei faction, anticipating inevitable dissolution, argued that such a resolution would lead to unavoidable conflict between the Diet and the government. However, the general sentiment within the party was relatively strong. Recently, the Tohoku Diet members group, led by Tokutake, which hoped to establish a Tohoku revitalization budget, and a faction that disapproved of using the Meicho issue for political strife, took action to shift towards a dissolution-supporting movement. President Suzuki's health also subtly influenced the dissolution-leaning argument within the Seiyukai, making the party's direction uncertain. Meanwhile, the Minseito party aimed to solidify its party position by aligning with the Seiyukai's Chen Rong. The party decided that the local elections should be a purge and an election to realize government policies, thus coordinating with the government on the same front, ensuring a majority of pro-government personnel. The military naturally hoped for dissolution. While dissolution would inevitably delay the budget's approval, it would certainly be established in a special session. Therefore, numerous issues related to the military remained unresolved, such as the military control problem, budget formulation disputes, the Kokutai Meicho issue, and informal statements regarding understanding the international situation. Thus, there seemed to be an intention to avoid escalating conflict with the government through Diet dissolution. Consequently, considering the circumstances from all sides, the atmosphere strongly favored dissolution. (25th Electric Communications Society dispatch)

House of Representatives Selects Committee Chairs; Mostly Dominated by the Seiyukai 44

Tokyo: The House of Representatives decided on the standing committee chairs for the budget, settlement of accounts, petitions, proposals, and disciplinary matters on the 27th. In the previous session, due to cooperation between the Seiyukai and Minseito parties, the two parties each held half the positions. However, the cooperation was canceled in May, intensifying the confrontation between the two parties. Therefore, the Seiyukai, wielding its absolute majority, monopolized all the committee chairs. The drafting committee chair for the Imperial Rescript's response is currently deliberating on candidates. (25th Electric Communications Society dispatch)

Japan and Canada Restore Trade Relations; Retaliatory Tariffs to be Abolished from January Next Year 45

Tokyo: The House of Peers factions' negotiation meeting was held on the afternoon of the 24th at the research association office. They decided on candidates for the full House committee chair and standing committee members. The candidate for the full House committee chair was Toshiaki Tokugawa (Kayokai), the budget committee chair was Yasusada Yanagisawa (Kenkyukai), and the vice-chair was Kiyotaka Chiaki. (25th Nichiren Association dispatch)

Tokyo: The temporarily deteriorated Japan-Canada trade relations have had a supportive opportunity since the establishment of Mr. Kanaya's Liberal Party cabinet. Recently, the ambassador to Canada negotiated with Prime Minister Kanaya, and opinions on opening up trade relations between the two countries have reached a consensus. From New Year's Day next year, the two governments will abolish retaliatory tariffs and restore the situation before the invocation of the Trade Protection Act in late July. This decision will not take the form of a Japan-Canada trade agreement but will be achieved by Canada amending its domestic laws, aiming to ease inappropriate measures against Japan by January 1st next year. Simultaneously, Japan has also decided to cancel the invocation of the Trade Protection Act. All procedures for abolishing the Imperial Ordinance regarding the Trade Protection Act will be completed at the Tariff Investigation Council on the 26th and seconded at the cabinet meeting on the 27th, which will then be notified to Canada. (25th Electric Communications dispatch)

Japan Allied News Agency Begins New News Dispatches; Grand Alliance of Domestic and Overseas News Agencies; Government and Public Join Forces to Strengthen News Presence 46

Tokyo: Japan's largest news agency, named the Allied News Agency, has decided to begin news dispatches on January 1, 1936. The Ministry of Communications has convened a meeting of influential figures from major news agencies to discuss various operational issues, deciding on the following three principles:

* The agency will be an independent and unbiased news organization.

* It will unite various domestic and overseas news agencies and broadcasting associations in Japan to create the strongest news presence in Japan.

* It will gather and disseminate various news from the standpoint of the Japanese Empire.

Major news agencies such as the United Electric and Communications Agency will also join the cooperation. Currently, over ninety news agencies have joined. The responsible personnel selected by the agency are as follows:

Acting President and Director: Miyokichi Tanaka. "Directors": Hochi (Shiro Terada), To-O (Kan'ichiro Yamada), Tokyo Nichi Nichi (Koki Okazaki), Tokyo Asahi (Takeo Ogata), Chugai (Miyokichi Tanaka), Otaru (Ikuzaburo Yagami), Osaka Mainichi (Shingo Takaishi), Osaka Asahi (Hiroshi Shimomura), Yomiuri (Matsutaro Shoriki), Kobe (Tsunehiko Wada), Kochi (Kusukichi Nonaka), Kokumin (Hitoshi Tanaka), Sanyo (Saichi Okamoto), Kyoto (Fumio Yamane), Kyushu Nichi Nichi (Hisashi Morita), Shinano Mainichi (Takeo Kosaka), Jiji (Masao Matsuoka), Shin-Aichi (Ukichi Oshima), Broadcasting Corporation (Shichiro Komori, Tatsuketsu Nakayama, Naotaro Yamamoto, Gentaro Ogino, Kinshitsu Yakuta). American Newspaper Comments on Lindbergh's Trip to Europe; Considers it a National Disgrace; Concerns About Inadequate Protection; Great Man Leaving the Country is Akin to Being Exiled 48

New York: The Lindbergh couple's move to England has been criticized by newspapers across the United States, considering it a disgrace to the United States. The New York Communications Newspaper stated that although there have been cases of great men leaving their countries in the past, no country has ever forced its most famous figure to move abroad out of fear for their life due to inadequate protection. The New York Times stated that "We must resolutely eliminate the thugs in the country and allow Lindbergh and the children of ordinary citizens to live safely in the country." (25th Reuters dispatch)

New York: Today's evening newspapers are filled with comments on Colonel Lindbergh's family trip to England. The Scripps-Howard newspapers stated that since the Lindbergh kidnapping law was implemented, there have been fifty-five kidnapping cases nationwide, all but two of which have been solved. One hundred and twenty-two kidnappers have been convicted, four of whom have received the death penalty and the rest sentenced to imprisonment. "As for Lindbergh's personal lack of opinions, others cannot interfere, but we believe it is unnecessary." The Kansas City Star stated, "Lindbergh is virtually being exiled from America, a national disgrace." The New York Daily News, while acknowledging Lindbergh's move as an escape from thugs, stated, "However, his own efforts to avoid official reports are sufficient to generate publicity, similar to the movie star Garbo." (24th National Electric dispatch)

Liverpool: The police department here stated today that when Colonel Lindbergh's family arrives here next week, the police department does not intend to provide special protection. (24th National Electric dispatch)

New York: Regarding the famous aviator Colonel Lindbergh's trip to Europe, the Daily News recently reported that Hauptmann, the culprit in the Lindbergh kidnapping case, has repeatedly been questioned by the court but has not confessed. It is unknown whether he will confess his crime out of remorse on his deathbed. Lindbergh originally planned to meet with Hauptmann briefly on January 13th next year, when Hauptmann was scheduled to be executed. However, after learning that New Jersey Governor Hoffman (who decided to request a retrial of the Hauptmann case) had secretly met with him in prison, he abandoned the original plan and followed his wife's wishes to travel to Europe. He is scheduled to fly back to the country by plane next spring. (24th Havas dispatch)

Two New York Banks, on Behalf of the Government, Buy Chinese and Indian Silver; Maintain Market Conditions to Prevent Impact of Silver Price Decline; Reportedly Purchased 50 Million Ounces from Our Country 49

London: Reuters has learned that the National City Bank of New York and the Chase National Bank have agreed to buy silver futures expiring in March in China and Bombay on behalf of the US government in order to maintain market conditions and prevent the serious impact of the silver price decline. According to reliable sources, the two banks have purchased 50 million ounces of silver from the Chinese government. After the news that foreign exchange was used to maintain the Chinese currency Mt. Aori silver market improved, sentiment became more optimistic. It is reported that speculators from China and India have slightly purchased. Some parties here believe that the recent manipulation of the silver market by the United States aims to control the power of the silver market in New York's hands. (25th Reuters dispatch)

Washington: Today, the Treasury Department announced that the government has purchased 761,774,000 ounces of silver as of December 6th, costing US$438,698,442, an average of 57 cents per ounce. The silver will be booked at $1.29 per ounce, so even though the current silver price has fallen, the government still has a surplus of $543,990,018 on its books. Currently, only 362,000,000 ounces have been booked as actual surplus, and the rest are calculated as silver ingots in inventory. However, once the banknotes are printed, they will also be used as reserves for the banknotes at a price of $1.29. The current number in the Treasury Department's inventory is 1,473,774,000 ounces, far from the target of 2,600,000,000 ounces. Therefore, some parties have begun to advocate for Congress to acknowledge that it is impossible to reach this target and change the law. (24th National Electric dispatch)

Tragic Car Crash in Berlin; 20 Dead, 80 Injured 52

Berlin: Last night, an express train departing from Berlin collided near Gross Kreutz with a train parked there, resulting in 20 deaths and 80 injuries. The scene was horrific, and the screams and moans of the injured shattered the silence of the winter night. Doctors and ambulances rushed to the scene after receiving the alarm. All the deaths were passengers on the train parked there. Passengers on the express train departing from Berlin were unharmed. The cause of the accident varies, with some saying that the express train ignored the warning signals, while others say that the switch operator mistakenly pulled the switch. Most of the victims were villagers who were traveling to visit relatives for the holidays. Unexpectedly, they encountered this disaster on the way. Christmas gifts and children's toys were scattered on both sides of the tracks. (25th Reuters dispatch)

French Literary Giant Paul Bourget Passes Away 54

Paris: The famous writer Paul Bourget recently passed away here at the age of 83. Bourget was born in 1852 and became a member of the Académie Française in 1895. He initially engaged in writing during his spare time as a professor and then devoted himself to literature. His two books, "Essays on Modern Psychology" (1883) and "New Essays" (1885), are known for their sharp criticism. Later, he turned his attention to novels, focusing on depicting the middle class and social issues. He produced a prolific body of work and was revered by the world. (25th Havas dispatch)

Train Crash at Caolaoji Station on the Tianjin-Pukou Railway; 3 Dead, 7 Injured; Driver on the Run 66

Xuzhou: A train crash occurred at Caolaoji Station on the Tianjin-Pukou Railway at 1:00 AM this morning. At the time, a No. 402 freight train was stopped at a switch outside the Yangqi (foreign flag) on the second track south of the station. The last section of the guard car had not yet entered the switch. The No. 305 passenger train sped into the station, went south beyond the station, and rammed the guard car out of the station for several miles, overturning it outside the track. Liu Shimin, the captain of the train crew, Song Jiaren, a member of the security team, and Zhou Junting, a flagman, were all killed in the crash. Seven people were injured. Zhang Su, the driver of the No. 305 train, fled after causing the accident. The railway immediately sent a rescue vehicle to repair the damage. Both northbound and southbound trains were delayed. The injured were transported to Xu City this afternoon. The bodies of Liu Shimin and others will be transported to Xu City tonight. Their families are already in Xu City preparing coffins. The situation is extremely tragic. It is said that the passengers on the No. 305 train were fortunate not to be injured, and the engine was slightly damaged. (25th special dispatch)

Nanjing: According to sources in the transportation sector, a freight train and a southbound train collided on the Tianjin-Pukou Railway at Caolaoji Station near Xuzhou at 1:00 AM on the 25th. Liu Shimin, the section chief of the guard car on the freight train, was injured in the collision and died before he could be rescued. Guangdong Plane Accident: Four Pilots Killed, Two Planes Destroyed, Losses Exceeding 200,000 98

Guangzhou Correspondence: At around 8 am on the 18th of this month, Wu Dequn, the leader of the third squadron of the Guangdong Air Force, led pilots Deng Xiexun, Cai Bingqiu, and Chen Jingting, etc., to conduct aerial combat drills as usual. Wu and Deng were riding "Foker" style fighter jets, while Cai and Chen were riding "Curtiss" style fighter jets. When the two planes rose to an altitude of 6,000 feet, Wu and Deng's fighter jet began to practice various attack techniques. After circling in the sky for a while, Cai and Chen's fighter jet, upon seeing this, recognized the Foker jet as a simulated enemy and accelerated to pursue. The "Foker" jet immediately evaded. At 9:30 am, the "Foker" jet turned back to attack the "Curtiss" jet and intended to repel the enemy, with a faster speed than before. The "Foker" jet also rushed forward like lightning. Due to carelessness at one moment, the planes collided with each other at an altitude of over 3,000 feet. Thick smoke erupted, and the fuel tanks of the two planes exploded in the air. The four pilots in the planes were unable to escape and were killed. In an instant, the two planes fell to an open area near the No. 3 Middle School playground on Dongsha Road, outside the eastern suburbs. When they landed, the two planes were still burning. Upon hearing the news, the Air Force Headquarters immediately telegraphed the fire department to send fire trucks to put out the fire. On one side, the department sent an ambulance and four paramedics to the scene to provide rescue. They saw that Squadron Leader Wu Dequn's limbs were incomplete, and one leg was blown hundreds of feet away. Deng Xiexun's entire body was charred. Cai and Chen were also in the plane, their heads were burned, their faces were blurry, and they could not be identified. Their abdomens and intestines flowed out. Their deaths were tragic. The personnel of the funeral company were hired to go to the scene to put the four in coffins. It is reported that Wu was from Dongjiang, and Deng, Cai, and Chen were all from Taishan County. The Air Force Department considers the four young men died in the line of duty and is deeply saddened. It has requested the Headquarters to provide generous compensation to the families. A public memorial service is scheduled for the 21st, and they will be buried in the Air Force Cemetery in Yunhe Ridge. It is found that the two new planes were recently purchased from foreign countries and are new-style fighter jets, worth more than 200,000 yuan in total. (December 19th)

——Students Request Huang Huabiao to Maintain School Affairs

Unexpectedly, more than 40 students followed him shortly after he arrived at the college, immediately cut off communication, and rushed into the dean's office to search for Dean Li. At that time, some professors and school staff lost their freedom. The students rushed into the office of Director Yang of Gao Nong, ordered Director Yang Yinong to leave the school, and ordered him to confess the whereabouts of Dean Li. In this chaotic state, Dean Li felt that he could not carry out school affairs."

Talks on Rural Life 100

—Edited by Yu Qingtang

Mountain Residence on the East Bank of the Tong River, by Yang Yishui

1. The Mountain People on the East Bank of the Congshan Junling Tong River Still Linger in a Semi-Savage State

Speaking of the Tong River, everyone may be very unfamiliar, right? Well then, let's start from the Shanghai that everyone is familiar with and take the Shanghai-Hangzhou railway train to Hangzhou. Hangzhou is on the west bank of the Qiantang River. The Qiantang River tide in August, everyone may be very familiar with the name Qiantang River, right? Well then, how about we travel in this familiar Qiantang River now? Let's hire a small boat in Hangzhou first. Going upstream along the Qiantang River, it will only take half a day, and you can enjoy the landscape of the Fuchun River. If we move forward again, we can see that the green high mountains on both sides of the river are gradually approaching. In the middle of the high mountains on both sides, there seems to be a gap specially reserved for this river. This is the Tong River we are going to talk about.

There are six counties on both sides of the Tong River. The west bank is Fuyang, Xindeng, Tonglu, and Jiande, and the east bank is Zhuji and Pujiang. The counties of Tonglu and Jiande span the Tong River. What we are talking about now is the east bank of the Tong River, which is the junction of the three counties of Tong, Jian, and Pu.

Now let's disembark here and land.

Landing here, I am afraid you will feel very hard—there are no rickshaws after landing, nor are there sedan chairs or horses. We must walk the rest of the way ourselves. Because from here forward, all we see in front of us are mountains—the road we are taking is夹 between these thousands of mountains and valleys, or on the sheep intestine path winding around the Congshan Junling. You may be thinking, have we already arrived in Taoyuan? Yes—we are going to see a village every five or ten miles along the way. They are built at the foot of the mountain or on the mountainside. Cooking smoke often lingers on the rocks, and the sounds of chickens and dogs can sometimes be heard in our ears. Taoyuan is really a bit similar—however, if we take a closer look, we will break our impression of Taoyuan. Those are not tile houses inhabited by humans—those are animal dens made of茅草 and蓬蒿—this is not Taoyuan, but the world of mountain people lingering in a semi-savage state.

2. Every Inch of Land at the Feet of the Mountain People Belongs to the Mountain Owners

The mountain people do not eat rice, but mainly糊 made of苞萝 flour and soup made of沉淀 and soaked 蕨根. There is a great lack of mountain fields, and grain and rice naturally become very precious things. The seasonings are vegetables grown on the mountain land and wild vegetables that grow naturally on the mountain. The mountain is really convenient for them—of course they also raise pigs and chickens, but they do not eat the meat of these pigs and chickens themselves. What do they raise them for? They also rarely plant one or two acres of mountain fields, and of course grain comes out of the fields, but they do not eat it themselves either. What do they grow it for? They sometimes go to the mountains to plant or采发, and sometimes they also make tools in their own homes. They must have the skills of both farmers and craftsmen. But their planting,采发, and production are not free. Why is this? You must have questions.

Because when the mountain people open the door, all the green mountains they see are not their own—many, even the thatched cottage they live in is not their own—every plant and tree in the mountain, every tile on the roof (it is茅草—), every inch of soil under their feet belongs to the mountain owners dozens or hundreds of miles away—

3. The Mountain Owners, in Order to Make Every Drop Return to Their Own Warehouses, Are Powerful People Driving the Mountain People

Most of the mountain owners live in small, flat plains where the mountain ridges are not very crowded. Because it is a small plain, the roads are naturally flatter. The geographical situation makes this small plain a market for primitive exchange by mountain farmers. The mountain owners who live on this small plain are mostly shop owners in this market and landlords on the small plain. They are the masters of the verdant, rolling mountains in the distance, and also the masters of the fate of these mountain farmers.

The mountain owner's ownership of the mountain塲 is the same as the landlord's ownership of the land. The only difference is: "Rich families manage the fields, and powerful families manage the mountains." The mountain owner must add a little "豪" to "富". Because, in general, the distance from the mountain塲 to the owner's home is often farther than the distance from the land to the owner. In order to make every drop in the mountain return to the mountain owner's warehouse, it is naturally necessary to be more powerful than ordinary landlords. Moreover, because the mountain塲 cannot be as flat and unshielded as the land, and the boundaries are clear and not mixed, it is necessary to have a commanding arrogance in order to make the mountain farmers obey.

The high mountains cannot send the resources in the mountains to the mountain owner's door by themselves. The mountain owner must have mountain people to plant and采发 on the mountains, bring them home to manufacture, and transport them to the mountain owner's home. Therefore, in the first step, the mountain owner must first make a selection of the mountain塲: which place can be planted? Which place can be探发? In general, the soil that is thick and more can be planted with苞萝 and tung trees, called杉木山, and the soil that is thin and more stone can only be used for burning charcoal from firewood in the mountain, called柴　山. The mountain owner is based on this standard and then either leases it to the mountain people to plant or orders the mountain people to采发. Then, the natural wealth夹 with the sweat and blood of the mountain people is transported in baskets and baskets to their own warehouses.

What kind of纽带 is used to complete this process? Below we will explain this kind of纽带 between the mountain owner and the mountain people, and the process completed by this纽带.

A mountain owner has a mountain, just like a landlord has a square field, and the rent is collected in the same way. We have already said that there is no difference. However, there is one thing that is different between mountains and fields, that is, the crops on the mountains cannot be harvested every year like the fields. The harvest on the mountains decreases year by year. After six or seven years, this planted mountain must be abandoned to restore the fertility of the mountain塲. This is a bit like the three-field system in primitive society. The production technology is low, and they do not know how to fertilize. After a long time, it will naturally become barren. In the eyes of the mountain owner, the turnover of the mountain's capital and profit is slower than that of the field. Therefore, the mountain tenancy system also differs greatly from the field. (To be continued)

Page 7

Li Shi Ci, Seriously Wounded and Passed Away, Cause of Attack Definitely Not a Personal Vendetta, Hong Kong Authorities Offer Reward for Arrest of Culprit 101

Hong Kong Dispatch: Li Gongyin, editor-in-chief of the Industrial and Commercial Daily, was suddenly attacked by assassins on Li Yuan East Street on the 16th of this month, suffering serious gunshot wounds. Police sent him to the National Hospital for treatment. After Mr. Li was admitted to the hospital, his condition fluctuated between improving and worsening. However, he ultimately succumbed to his injuries and passed away at 5:05 AM on the 20th. The details are recorded below:

Continuous Deterioration of Condition: After Mr. Li entered the hospital, his temperature and pulse rate had slightly decreased by the afternoon of the 16th. However, because both his small and large intestines had been penetrated by bullets, his condition remained extremely serious. By late evening on the 16th, he felt increasingly uncomfortable, and fecal matter was vomited from his mouth. He felt somewhat better after doctors performed a gastric lavage. On the 17th, Mr. Li's colleagues visited him in the hospital and found his spirit and complexion had improved. His voice was also quite strong as he thanked his colleagues for their concern. On the 18th, his condition was slightly more serious than before. From midnight, his pulse was 120 beats per minute and his temperature was 106 degrees Fahrenheit. He groaned incessantly, tossed and turned in bed, and frequently cried out in pain. He was able to fall asleep only after Dr. Tan performed a gastric lavage and administered an injection. At 3 PM, Mr. Li's younger brother and mother visited him. Mr. Li's expression had greatly improved, and he had a detailed conversation with his brother, encouraging him, and comforted his mother. At 4 PM, his pulse was 125 beats per minute and his temperature was 99.4 degrees Fahrenheit. However, he looked slightly fatigued. From 6 PM to 8 PM, his condition suddenly deteriorated. He vomited several times in those two hours, expelling clots and yellowish-white foul liquid, about three or four mouthfuls. He also felt short of breath, like he was about to vomit, and groaned in pain. At 7:30 PM, Dr. Tan performed another gastric lavage on Li. The reporter, with Dr. Tan's permission, accompanied the doctor on a visit. Although Mr. Li was groaning in pain, he was able to say, "I am very uncomfortable. If I vomit again, I will have no strength left." The reporter approached and offered comfort, and Mr. Li nodded in response. Then, he gestured for the reporter to leave. At 8:05 PM, after Dr. Tan and Mr. Li finished the gastric lavage, the reporter accompanied Li's brother for another visit. Upon seeing the reporter, Mr. Li immediately told his brother, "I will not die. You must work hard for your future, cherish your time, and be filial to our mother. There is no need to worry about me, I will not die." He also said that after the gastric lavage, his body felt more comfortable than before. The reporter later learned from the attending physician that Mr. Li's condition was still not out of danger. Based on the situation this evening (the 18th), his condition was more serious than the previous day. Although Mr. Li's temperature had not increased, there was no fear of inflammation. However, the doctor did not know the extent of internal organ damage based on the foul liquid that Mr. Li had vomited. In conclusion, the doctor could not say that Mr. Li's condition had improved. They still had to wait and see what happened in the next few days to determine his future. On the 19th, his condition worsened again. From 2 AM, he vomited until dawn, spitting out clotted blood, and was in extreme pain. According to the doctor, there was a fear that blood vessels were bleeding inside his abdomen, causing clotted blood to accumulate there. Therefore, another operation was necessary to remove the clotted blood in order to be effective. Re-operating would offer a glimmer of hope, while not operating would lead to despair. However, Mr. Li's family feared that his body could not withstand another operation. After the first operation, they felt that his expression had changed dramatically. If he underwent another operation, he would certainly not be able to endure it. Regarding the question of whether to operate again, the hospital doctors left the decision to his family. His family had no opinion and consulted a female doctor about everything, as she had assisted during the first operation to remove the bullets. In the end, no further surgery was performed. Mr. Li became more breathless that day. According to his family, since vomiting yesterday morning (the 18th), his throat felt strangely itchy and as hot as fire. At 2 AM on the 20th, Mr. Li felt even more pain, and his condition became even more dangerous. He lost his composure and his speech became incoherent. Despite the doctors' best efforts to save him, they were unable to turn the tide. At 5:05 AM, he unfortunately passed away. According to hospital sources, when doctors discovered that Mr. Li had lost consciousness at 2 AM on the 20th, they gave him a cardiac stimulant injection, and he soon fell asleep. However, at 4:50 AM, he struggled violently due to severe pain and was unable to speak. Approximately 20 minutes later, he passed away. During his final moments, he said to his brother that he had always treated people with sincerity and had no personal enemies. He said that judging from his injuries, he did not expect to live much longer and hoped that his colleagues in the newspaper would continue their efforts.

Funeral Arrangements: After Mr. Li passed away, the hospital immediately sent his remains to the mortuary. He was placed in a coffin at 2:30 PM and the funeral procession departed at 3 PM, led by the National Hospital. He was buried at the foot of the mountain in the Western Chicken Cage Ring of Pok Fu Lam Road. Many relatives and friends sent wreaths, and hundreds of people attended the funeral procession, including many colleagues from Hong Kong newspapers. They bid farewell to his spirit at the farewell pavilion. It was raining and snowing that day, and the scene was extremely tragic. The pallbearers, remembering Mr. Li's 20 years as a journalist and his tragic death, were all deeply saddened. Mr. Li left behind an elderly mother and a wife, as well as children. His mother was heartbroken by her beloved son's tragic death, and her cries nearly caused her to faint.

Impoverished After Death: Mr. Li was generous throughout his life. He always did his best to help relatives and friends who sought his assistance. He often gave away half of his monthly salary to relatives and friends, leaving him penniless and impoverished after his death. He left behind a 70-year-old mother, a widow, and orphans waiting to be fed. The future is long, and this is truly the greatest sorrow in the world. The Hong Kong and mainland newspapers, along with his relatives and friends, have issued funeral announcements, hoping that Mr. Li's relatives and friends will offer condolences, and that all funeral gifts will be converted into cash, so that the deceased can rest in peace and the living can receive practical benefits.

Cause of Attack: Mr. Li was known to be upright, honest, and extremely kind. All of his colleagues in Hong Kong newspapers knew this, and they all deeply believed that Mr. Li had no personal enemies. So why was he shot by assassins? According to general observation, the newspaper Mr. Li oversaw had always vehemently condemned malicious forces without reservation. The Hong Kong newspapers were able to report relatively freely, and this greatly angered authorities from a certain quarter. These authorities had special agencies to deal with dissidents in Hong Kong and Macau. It is recalled that Luo Weijiang, the president of the Hong Kong Tiannan Daily, supported the Central Government and also strongly criticized certain authorities. Last year, he was shot as a result. Although Li did not support the Central Government, he was also dissatisfied with certain authorities. Therefore, his murder is similar to Luo's shooting last year. However, Luo was fortunate to survive, while Li died, making it a matter of fortune and misfortune.

Reward for Arrest of Culprit: The Hong Kong Police Authorities, considering that Li Yuan East Street is a prosperous area in the central district, were shocked that assassins dared to act so audaciously and commit murder in broad daylight. Therefore, after Mr. Li's death, they offered a reward of 250 yuan to arrest the murderers and bring them to justice. (21st)

Shandong Province Year-End Finances: Deficit of More Than 2.3 Million Yuan, Caused by Floods and Economic Decline 102

Jinan Dispatch: In recent years, the local situation in this province has been stable, the government has been reorganized, and revenues and expenditures have been balanced. However, this year, we suddenly encountered misfortune. The western half of Shandong suffered severe flooding, and various tax revenues fell sharply. As of the end of January of the 25th year (end of the lunar year), the estimated shortfall was 1.95 million yuan in revenue and 2.836 million yuan in expenditure, along with 600,000 yuan borrowed from treasury bonds before the busy farming season this year, totaling approximately 1.486 million yuan. Furthermore, from February to March of the 25th year, the estimated revenue was 9.7 million yuan and the expenditure was 10.594 million yuan, resulting in an additional shortfall of 894,000 yuan. Combining this with the previous shortfall from January, the total shortfall was over 2.38 million yuan. The Finance Department announced four reasons for this year's deficit: The floods in western Shandong affected over a dozen counties, causing severe damage and resulting in a shortfall of over 900,000 yuan in land tax revenue. Deed tax was a major source of revenue in previous years, but this year, due to economic decline in rural areas and low purchasing power among the people, there was a shortfall of approximately 500,000 yuan. Due to the sluggish market and economic downturn, business tax revenue fell short by over 180,000 yuan. Repayment of principal and interest on loans from the Sino-Japanese Industrial Company amounted to over 790,000 yuan. The total deficit is as stated above. Wang Xiangrong, the Director of the Finance Department, presented this case at the provincial government's political affairs meeting on the 24th, requesting a solution to make up the deficit. It was decided to hand the case over to the Secretariat, the four departments, the judicial department, and the committee for review and research of methods to cover the deficit. (24th)

Italy's Economic Crisis: Exports Sharply Decline, Economic Prospects Cause Concern; Domestic Prices Soar, People Panic; Impact of the League of Nations' Economic Sanctions 104

Rome Dispatch: The economic sanctions imposed by the League of Nations officially began on November 18th. It is widely known that Britain played the most active role in Geneva to ensure the implementation of these sanctions. The reason given for this is the ostensibly praiseworthy [stopping aggressive behavior]. However, when our Northeast Four Provinces were ravaged, we repeatedly requested the League of Nations to implement sanctions, but we never heard anyone championing justice like Britain at that time make any pronouncements. Today's situation is also due to conflicts of interest among the great powers, who are using this Geneva body as a tool to deal with each other. Although it sets a precedent that we can use in the future to demand that League of Nations member states also impose sanctions on those who aggress against our country, it is still highly questionable whether the current movement is based on justice. We will not discuss the background of the movement any further. In terms of the economic sanctions currently being implemented, Italy is suffering a great impact. Italy is located on a peninsula, with only the Lombardy area bordering France, Austria, and Switzerland being plains. The rest is either mountainous or barren. Mineral resources are scarce, and raw material production is extremely limited, relying heavily on imports from abroad. Currently, among the League of Nations member states, except for Austria, Hungary, Albania, and Uruguay, the remaining thirty-eight countries are participating in unreserved economic sanctions against Italy. Another thirteen countries are implementing economic sanctions against Italy with reservations. According to the principles of economic sanctions, all cannot import raw materials and mineral products into Italy. If we look at global production, essential raw materials are produced in countries that are implementing sanctions against Italy. From the above figures, we can see that most of the raw materials and minerals needed by Italy are in countries that are implementing economic sanctions against Italy, ranging from 100% to 73%. As for coal and oil, Italy imported over 117.8 million quintals of coal last year, mainly from the United Kingdom, Germany, and Poland. It also imported over 1.5 million quintals of oil, mainly from the Soviet Union, Persia, Romania, and the United States. Gasoline imports totaled 3.48 million quintals, mainly from Romania, the Dutch East Indies, and Persia and Romania. Except for the United States and Germany, which are not members of the League of Nations, the rest are participating in the economic sanctions against Italy. There is currently a proposal to add coal and oil to the sanctions list, which would inflict an even greater blow on Italy. Yesterday, the Italian Ministry of Foreign Affairs notified the foreign embassies in Italy that all oil, gasoline, sugar, and coffee, etc., that could previously be purchased duty-free, must be purchased directly from abroad by the embassies themselves. From December 15th, they will no longer be able to purchase them duty-free within Italy. This measure is a preliminary move to retaliate against countries imposing economic sanctions against Italy, and also to conserve the use of its domestic inventory. The application of gasoline is crucial for military aircraft, industrial activities, and transportation. If the source is cut off for even one day, the impact will be even greater than the food supply being cut off, hence this great panic.

From November 18th to the 28th, only ten days, it is still difficult to estimate the extent of the impact on Italy. However, soaring prices have become a very common phenomenon. Even daily necessities, except for bread and noodles, etc., cannot be avoided. It is universally acknowledged that life is becoming increasingly difficult here. It is generally known that the gold reserves and foreign exchange reserves of the Italian Bank (National Bank) have decreased by 25% in the past four months, about 430 million lire. If this continues, it will continue to decrease. If there is no improvement in military or diplomatic affairs, then, given this the people are in a state of panic or perhaps a more panic-stricken period will arrive. Therefore, many are tightening their belts to prepare for any eventuality, and some are even combining three meals into two. The situation can be seen at a glance. Government agencies have shortened office hours, and shops are following suit to save electricity. Elevators in households are either abandoned or only used for going up but not down, and cannot be remotely controlled from upper levels to go down and pick people up, etc. All of these are for saving money and electricity. It is said that public buses may be temporarily completely suspended to save gasoline, and trams will also reduce services, encouraging people to walk to and from, to help the country's economy. All of these are phenomena of the past ten days, indicating that it has already been deeply affected by economic sanctions. In addition, looking at Italy's overall trade situation, we can see that if economic sanctions continue to be implemented, Italy's economic and financial situation will be greatly affected. Last year, over 60% of Italy's goods exports were to countries that are currently implementing economic sanctions against Italy. These countries have now tightly closed their customs doors. It is not easy to find other countries as sales outlets in a short period of time. Here is a simple table to show Italy's export situation. If other outlets are sought, but there is still no quick and proper solution, then Italy's entire financial and economic future is very dangerous and worrying.

Local News

Tang Youren Assassinated Yesterday: Thugs Ambushed at Doorstep, Caught Unawares; Shot Three Times in Vital Areas, Died Instantly; Mayor Expresses Condolences to Family, Orders Strict Investigation of Assailants 105

Former Director-General of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and currently Standing Director-General of the Ministry of Communications and Advisor to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Mr. Tang Youren, was ambushed and shot by two thugs lurking at the rear gate steps of his residence at 235 Gan Village, Gan Shidong Road, French Concession, at around 4:45 PM yesterday as he returned from visiting guests. Mr. Tang was shot several times and died on the spot. The assailants all escaped. Mr. Tang's body has been moved to the Public Works Department Hospital on Tairas Road to await entombment. The French Police Department is taking this case very seriously. Details are reported below.

Arrival in Shanghai from Beijing

Mr. Tang Youren, former Vice Minister of Foreign Affairs and Secretary-General of the Central Political Council, resigned after the recent Sixth Plenary Session of the Central Executive Committee and the Fifth National Congress concluded and the ministers of the central government's ministries were re-elected. He was reappointed as Standing Director-General of the Ministry of Communications and Advisor to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. He arrived in Shanghai from Beijing on the night express train on the 23rd and returned to his private residence at 235 Gan Village, Gan Shidong Road, French Concession.

Visiting Wang Jingwei

After arriving at his residence in Shanghai on the morning of the day before yesterday, Mr. Tang visited Mr. Wang Jingwei at Anhe Temple Road in the afternoon and then returned to his residence. At 9:00 AM yesterday morning, he went out again by car (concession license number 6934, Chinese area license number 3150), first visiting Mr. Wang again. He returned to his residence for lunch and went out again at 1:00 PM, first visiting relatives and friends at Yuyuan Road, and then to Mr. Zhang Gongquan, the new Minister of Railways, at 705 Julieda Road.

Car Returning to Gan Village

Mr. Tang and Zhang Gongquan had a long private conversation and left at around 4:45 PM, ordering the driver to drive back to his residence. When the car arrived at the entrance of the lane in Gan Village, because Tang's residence was the third house in the lane, facing south and north, and the width of the lane was less than one zhang (about 3.3 meters), the car could not turn around. Therefore, when Tang's car arrived at the entrance of the lane, it reversed into the lane. When the car backed up to the back door, Mr. Tang got out of the car leisurely.

Thugs Attacking from Both Sides

After Mr. Tang got out of the car, he knocked on the back door twice, but no one opened the door. At this time, Tang's youngest son was inside and asked loudly when he heard the sound, "Is Daddy back?" Tang replied, "Yes." Unexpectedly, before Tang finished answering, two thugs wearing gray-yellow breeches and overcoats rushed out from the front and back of the car, pulled out pistols, and attacked Mr. Tang from both sides. When Mr. Tang saw that the situation was not good, he quickly turned around and took large steps onto the cement steps, intending to escape into the back door on the second floor.

Double Guns Firing Simultaneously

The cement steps at the back door of Tang's residence have thirteen steps, leading directly to the back door on the second floor. At that time, Mr. Tang had just stepped onto the third step when the two thugs could no longer wait and aimed their guns at him and fired simultaneously, firing a total of eight or nine shots. Mr. Tang was less than five steps away, so he was shot three times all over his body, and all were vital areas. However, Mr. Tang was still a strong young man and finally managed to climb to the top of the steps and pushed against the back door, shouting for help. Coincidentally, when Mr. Tang knocked on the back door downstairs after getting out of the car, and at the same time Tang's youngest son asked loudly, a female relative on the second floor had already heard Tang knocking on the back door downstairs, thinking that Tang had already entered from the back door downstairs, and never expected that Tang would encounter violence downstairs and escape to the second floor.

Barely Alive

It was not until the female relative heard the continuous gunshots and Tang shouting for help outside the door that she realized something was wrong. By the time she opened the door, Tang had already fallen into the back door in a pool of blood. At the same time, Tang's wife, Ouyang Liwei (the sister of the famous playwright Ouyang Yuqian), was sitting on the bed because she had been feeling unwell for several days. Suddenly hearing the gunshots, she knew that something had happened. By the time she put on her shoes and ran out, Tang was already lying in a pool of blood. When he saw his wife, he could only open his mouth to signal, barely alive.

Assailants Escaped

At that time, Tang's chauffeur witnessed the thugs firing and was so frightened that he was stunned. After the thugs ran away and escaped, he regained his composure and got out of the car to report to a Vietnamese policeman at the corner of Gan Shidong Road. By the time the policeman arrived, the thugs had already disappeared without a trace. At this time, Tang's wife quickly helped Tang onto the car and rushed him to Niu Huilin Hospital. After Dr. Niu examined him, he determined that all three shots were in vital areas. One bullet entered from the right flank and exited from the left armpit, one bullet entered from the right waist but did not penetrate, and one bullet entered from the right buttock and penetrated the left hip. Dr. Niu determined that there was no hope of survival.

Died from Serious Injuries

He then ordered him to be rushed to Guangci Hospital, but the hospital refused to admit him because no police officers accompanied him. He had no choice but to be transferred to the Lugiawan General Police Station. At this time, Tang's eyeballs only made a final glance before he was pronounced dead from serious injuries. Seeing that Tang had died, the police station ordered him to be sent to the Public Works Department Hospital (i.e., the small ward) on Tairas Road and placed in the attached mortuary, awaiting a report to the Second Special Court to send someone to examine the body.

Strict Investigation of Assailants

After the incident, the French Police Department dispatched Chinese and foreign detectives to Tang's residence for a thorough investigation, collected all the bullet casings dropped by the thugs, recorded them, and kept them for future reference. According to the chauffeur's statement, there were indeed three assailants at the time, but only two acted. Several hours before the incident, a red sedan was seen parked there for a long time. After the incident, the car disappeared. At the same time, Mayor Wu Tiecheng also received a report and immediately sent Secretary Geng Jiaji to Tang's residence to express condolences, and then went to the French Consulate General and the French Police Department to request a strict investigation of the fugitives. At the same time, the municipal government ordered the Municipal Public Security Bureau to assist in the strict investigation. At the same time, Tang's residence telegraphed to the central government and Tang's brother, Bu Nian, and his younger brother, Gui Liang, to come to Shanghai to take charge of the funeral arrangements.

Tang's Background

Tang's name is Lin, 42 years old, from Liuyang, Hunan. He is a revolutionary veteran and the second son of Tang Caichang. His mother is still alive. He studied in Shanghai in his early years and then went to Japan to study law at Keio University, where his academic performance was outstanding among his peers and was praised by teachers and friends. After graduating in the eighth year of the Republic (1919), he returned to China and was recruited by the Bank of China to preside over the Economic Investigation Office, focusing on research on finance and economics, and made many contributions to the Bank of China. In the seventeenth year of the Republic (1928), the Bank of China headquarters moved south, so he came to Shanghai. When Tang was in Japan, due to his family background, he had many contacts with Kuomintang comrades, and was especially valued by veterans such as Chiang Kai-shek and Wang Jingwei. After coming to Shanghai, he traveled back and forth frequently, and quickly distinguished himself. Therefore, when Wang Jingwei also served as Minister of Foreign Affairs, he recruited Tang to assist him. During his more than two years in office, he adhered to the central government's diplomatic policies, shouldering the important responsibility of negotiation, and did not complain about the hard work, bearing both praise and criticism. Tang sought the best for the nation and the clan, and should have no regrets at the moment. However, he repeatedly applied to the party and national authorities for resignation and distant travel, but was not granted permission. Friends, seeing Tang's difficult situation and the difficulty in distinguishing right from wrong, advised Tang to be vigilant, but Tang remained indifferent, so he suffered this misfortune. He left behind two sons and two daughters. The eldest daughter, San Cheng, is only ten years old, the second daughter, Lian Cheng, is six years old, the eldest son, Wencheng, is seven years old, and the youngest son, Man Cheng, is four years old. It is faintly heard that Tang recently purchased land on Guanyintang Road in the downtown area to build a new mansion, magnificent and about to be completed. Unexpectedly, he has already suffered this tragedy.

Photograph of Tang Youren

Student Petitioners Arrive in Kunshan and Suzhou; A Group of Students Returned to Shanghai Last Night; Enduring Hardships in Rain and Snow; Beijing and Shanghai Should Avoid [Conflict] and Offer Joint Comfort; Tongji Students Returned First Last Night 106

A Central News Agency report states that the two trains carrying petitioning students, which departed from the North Station the day before yesterday (24th) afternoon, arrived at Kunshan Station around 8 or 9 PM that night. The first train was mostly filled with students from Fudan University, with the remainder from Guangxia Middle School, China Middle School, Jianguo Middle School, Shibei Middle School, and other schools, totaling about six or seven hundred people. The second train was almost entirely composed of students from Tongji University and Xiangji Senior Vocational School, numbering four or five hundred. The students on the first train forced the driver to proceed to Suzhou. Yesterday morning, they further compelled the stationmaster in Suzhou to order the driver to depart, but due to damaged tracks, they had to stop at Wangting Station. The students from Tongji University and the vocational school on the second train were also quite enthusiastic. Initially, they were delayed due to a lack of a locomotive. Later, when a third and fourth-class train arrived in Kunshan from Beijing, the students immediately forced the driver to attach the locomotive to their train cars, preparing to depart. However, Li Dachao, the chief of the First Section of the Municipal Government, had already led several officials from the Municipal Government and the Bureau of Education, rushing to Kunshan Station overnight, repeatedly dissuading them. The Shanghai Municipal Security Force also deployed to Kunshan Station to maintain order, awaiting further instructions. As a result, the third and fourth-class passenger train and the student train cars remained deadlocked and were unable to depart. Peng Baichuan, the magistrate of Kunshan County, acting on orders from the Jiangsu Provincial Government, received the students, providing food and drink. At night, rain and snow fell heavily, and the weather turned abruptly cold, but the students' spirits remained high. At 10:30 AM yesterday morning, Pan Gongzhan, the Director of the Municipal Bureau of Education, accompanied by Ma Zongrong, a special secretary dispatched by the Ministry of Education to Shanghai by plane, along with Jiang Jianbai, the Director of the Education Bureau, and over ten officials from the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Bureau of Education, rushed to Kunshan. They first consulted with Magistrate Peng, and then proceeded to the station with Chief Li and others. They began by earnestly explaining the government's intentions to several representatives of the Tongji students, and then urged all the students to disembark and form a line on the platform. Secretary Ma, Director Pan, Chief Li, and others sincerely persuaded and explained with heartfelt words and tears. They also promised to relay all the petition requests to the central government. The students were deeply moved. Wang Zuozhou and Jing Zhide, representatives of the Tongji Senior Vocational School National Salvation Association, first stated on behalf of their classmates that they would comply with President Jiang's repeated telegrams of encouragement. Because the authorities' persuasion was sincere and earnest, because the second and fourth-class passenger trains had been delayed for a day and a night, causing deep unease, and because the tracks ahead were damaged, making it impossible to proceed further and staying in Kunshan would be futile, they expressed their willingness to return to Shanghai immediately. However, they hoped that Director Pan and others would relay their six demands to the central government for adoption: 1. Oppose the puppet autonomous region in North China; 2. Safeguard territorial integrity; 3. Ban and revise textbooks in North China; 4. Punish those who suppress students' patriotic movements; 5. Provide compensation to injured students in North China; 6. Punish traitors like Yin Rugeng. This request was granted. Subsequently, Weng Zhilong, the President of Tongji University, along with professors and students' parents, arrived in Kunshan by train to jointly offer comfort. The university students also decided to return to school as a group, showing their sincere patriotism and refusing to be exploited by external forces. Director Pan, Secretary Ma, President Weng, and others were very pleased. They boarded the train with the students back to Shanghai. At that time, the third and fourth-class passenger train had already departed. When the student train left Kunshan, it was already 6:30 PM. This train went directly to Jiangwan and Wusong, where the students disembarked in two groups. It did not stop at any other stations. By 7:30 PM, the Tongji students had safely arrived at their school. As for Fudan University, President Li, Secretary-General Jin, and various professors reportedly also went to Suzhou in batches yesterday to persuade their students to return to Shanghai. It is expected that this train will be able to return to Shanghai from between Wuxi and Suzhou today. The details of what happened are recorded as follows:

Two Trains Coupled Together Arrive in Kunshan and Suzhou

Around 5 PM the night before last, the students petitioning in Beijing, departing from the North Station, numbered over 2,300. At that time, the railway bureau coupled them into two trains. The first train had nine first, second, and third-class cars, and the second train had eight first, second, and third-class cars. As the trains departed and arrived at Kunshan, both drivers disembarked and fled one after another. The male and female students were in angry uproar. Then, a student on the first train, with some mechanical knowledge, boldly took on the role of driving. The other students feared there might be obstacles on the tracks, so they obtained a track inspection car to precede them. Thereupon, this train, sounding its horn, proceeded towards Suzhou. As it passed through Zhengyi Station, it had a minor dispute with the stationmaster because its request for waybills was not granted. Suzhou Station, having received the above news, once dismantled a section of the track, but the students managed to overcome this obstacle. The second train remained stationary at Kunshan Station. At 7 PM on the 25th, a telegram from Suzhou stated that the student petition train departed Suzhou westward at 4 PM on the 25th. At Xushuguan, the railway bureau had preemptively dismantled the track, preventing the train from proceeding further. The Ministry of Education dispatched two supervisors, Zhao and Ma, to Suzhou to persuade the students to return to Shanghai.

The Beijing Municipal Bureau is Persuading in Different Routes

Over two thousand petitioning students from various schools in Shanghai were ordered westward by the authorities the night before last, with the intention of persuading them to return to Shanghai. However, the students firmly refused, resulting in two trains, one stopping at Kunshan and the other at Suzhou. The authorities believed that while the students' actions were admirable, if they all went to Beijing, students from other regions would inevitably follow suit. This would not only greatly impact transportation but also cause various inconveniences in Nanjing. Therefore, they continued to send personnel to explain with goodwill. The Ministry of Education dispatched Secretary Ma Zongrong, Supervisor Hao Gengsheng, and Sun Guofeng, who were sent to Shanghai to persuade the students. They departed yesterday morning at 7 AM, along with Li Dachao, the Chief of the First Section of the Municipal Government, Pan Gongzhan, the Director of the Municipal Bureau of Education, Li Denghui, the President of Fudan University, Jin Tongyin, the Secretary-General, and the relevant authorities from other schools, and went to Kunshan and Suzhou to persuade the students. Secretary Ma Zongrong of the Ministry of Education, Director Pan Gongzhan of the Municipal Bureau of Education, and Chief Li Dachao of the First Section of the Municipal Government were responsible for persuasion in Kunshan. Supervisor Hao Gengsheng of the Ministry of Education, Sun Guofeng, and President Li Denghui of Fudan University went to Suzhou to persuade the students. (East China News Agency)

Ma Zongrong Talks About Three Points

At 12:30 PM, Ma Zongrong and Pan Gongzhan gathered the Tongji students at Kunshan Station for a speech. Mr. Ma first briefly stated his purpose, then said that he was here on behalf of Minister Wang and had three points to explain to the students: Firstly, he was deeply uneasy about the students' disregard for the severe winter weather, camping in the open air, to participate in the national salvation movement. Therefore, he rushed here on behalf of the central government to offer comfort. Secondly, the government had already accepted all the students' opinions on national affairs expressed in their march and petition. To avoid the students' hardship in the cold journey, President Jiang had stipulated a method: before January 15, presidents of Shanghai universities would be gathered, and each school would send one to three student representatives to Beijing to jointly contribute and present their opinions on national salvation. Thirdly, if the students felt that the deadline was too far away and could not wait, the Ministry of Education had sent people like him to come first. If they had any opinions, they could submit them in writing or verbally to him so that he could forward them to Minister Wang, who would then forward them to President Jiang. As for the opinions previously raised, the central government had already fully understood them. However, the capacity of Beijing was limited. If all university students in the country wanted to go to Beijing, not only would the city be unable to accommodate them, but their studies would also be neglected, which would be a great pity. (National News Agency)

Pan Uses the Example of Students in North China

Director Pan Gongzhan of the Bureau of Education then earnestly advised, believing that the students in Peiping and Tianjin were in a more profound situation and faced greater stimulation than those in Shanghai. When the students went to Beijing to petition and were blocked in Cangzhou, the Ministry of Education, upon hearing the news, also sent representatives to offer comfort. As a result, the students and representatives spoke to the point of embracing and weeping together. At this time, the students also felt the nation's crisis and reluctantly returned. In short, at this time, it is necessary to bury oneself in hard work. If all students in the country went to Beijing at the same time, not only would their studies be affected, but the central government's work would also be impacted, which would not be a way to save the country. He hoped they would return. (National News Agency)

Mr. Zhang Taiyan Delivers a Speech

A telegram from Suzhou, New Voice News Agency, 7 PM on the 25th, states that Zhang Taiyan delivered a speech, expressing deep sympathy for the students' patriotic movement. However, he believed that the government authorities should handle it properly and should not rashly label them as communists or use force to stop them. He believed that the government and education authorities should be responsible for providing food to the hungry and cold students and taking good care of them along the way.

Tongji Students Return to School from Kunshan

Over three hundred students from Tongji University and its affiliated vocational and middle schools followed the Shanghai students to Beijing the night before last (24th). The train stopped at Kunshan Station and could not proceed. It was already late at night, and rain and snow were falling heavily. The students were both hungry and cold, and their situation was pitiful. The school authorities, upon hearing the news, were extremely anxious. They quickly purchased a large number of bread and canned food and hired cars to send them to where the students were staying. Yesterday morning around 10 AM, President Weng Zhilong, Secretary-General Du Dianying, Director Tang of the vocational school, Director Lu of the affiliated middle school, and over twenty faculty members departed from the school and temporarily negotiated with the North Station to request a special train to pick up the students and return them to school. The railway bureau approved the request, and the special train departed at 3 PM, arriving in Kunshan around 4 PM. They saw that the students, despite traveling through wind and snow, were in good order and full of vitality, showing their patriotic enthusiasm. At that time, Director Shen of the Municipal Bureau of Education led many officials from the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Bureau of Education, earnestly advising them. With the school authorities' sympathy and persuasion, the students understood the greater good and immediately held a meeting, deciding to return to school with the teachers. Around 6 PM, the train slowly returned to Shanghai, heading directly to Jiangwan and Wusong. By 7:30 PM, everyone had returned to their respective schools.

Affiliated Middle School of Fudan University Asks to Retain the President

Since hearing the news of President Li's resignation, all the teachers and students of the Affiliated Middle School of Fudan University have been deeply uneasy. Director Gu Yiwen personally went to persuade him yesterday morning. In the afternoon, a meeting of faculty members was convened, and it was unanimously decided to nominate Li Baiyuan, Leng Xueqiao, and Guo Zhiliang to present a letter of retention to President Li and request him to retract his resignation. The original letter is as follows: To President Denghui, Upon learning that you have expressed a desire to resign due to the student unrest in Shanghai, we are deeply uneasy. Our school has a history of thirty years, with an outstanding reputation and excellent achievements. Without your guidance, we would not have been able to achieve this. At this time of turbulent student unrest, the future of our school depends on your efforts to maintain it. After a unanimous decision by the faculty, Li Baiyuan and Leng Xueqiao are nominated to come and urge you to withdraw your resignation and continue to take on this difficult task. We hope that you will come to the school to give us instructions.

Jiaotong University Students Paraded Yesterday Morning

The National Salvation Association of Students of National Jiaotong University in this city, in order to shift public attention and arouse popular unity for national salvation, gathered over three hundred students from various colleges at 8 AM yesterday morning, organized them into a team, and departed from the school, passing through Longhua Road, Rihui Bridge, turning into Xietu Road, passing Xie Bridge, and entering the Republic of China Road, making a circum-city parade, shouting slogans along the way and extensively promoting national salvation to the public. The team was orderly and in good order. Around 1 PM, they returned to school and continued to attend classes as usual. There were no other unexpected incidents. (Shanghai News Agency)

Datong University Set Out for Propaganda

The private Datong University and Datong Affiliated Middle School in this city established a propaganda team, which departed yesterday morning in groups to propagate to the public in the areas of Zhonghua Road, Wenmiao Road, Minguo Road, Xiaodongmen, South Railway Station Road, and Laoximen. Each group consisted of twenty to thirty people, and many people gathered to watch. The students of the school also printed declarations and distributed them along the way. The content of the declaration was: resolutely deny all pseudo-organizations that undermine national integrity, recover the lost territories in Northeast and North China, execute all traitors and national criminals, request the government to protect patriotic movements throughout the country, unite patriotic organizations throughout the country, and unite all Chinese people to jointly face national crises. Around 4 PM, they gradually returned to school. (Shanghai News Agency)

China National Salvation Association Issues a Declaration

The China National Salvation Association convened its first standing committee meeting at 7 PM yesterday, chaired by the "Ta Kung Pao", to discuss several important cases and issued the following declaration: With the loss of the Northeast and the danger in North China, the traitor Yin Rugeng first betrayed the country, and then the pseudo-autonomous movement, falsely claiming popular opinion, arose. All revolutionary people are indignant. The students in Peiping, being in a dangerous situation, could not bear the loss of the motherland and rose up to save the country. The students in Shanghai were eager to save the country and dared not fall behind. In addition to marching and petitioning to express their will, they organized this association to engage in a sustained and arduous struggle. (Shanghai News Agency)
