Secondary Schools Obey the Order to Take a Holiday

Since the Bureau of Education issued an order for all secondary schools to take an early holiday, all schools have complied with the order yesterday and no classes were held. Reporters from Shanghai News Agency specifically inspected various schools in Nanshi yesterday, such as Wuben, Minli, Ai Qun, Jingye, Da Gong, Minli Girls' Middle School, Kaiming, Junyi, and Huadong. All of them had announced the holiday. Most of the day students did not come to school. Boarding students were picked up by their parents. Therefore, there were many vehicles in front of each school, carrying luggage. Students from other places who were on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway were unable to return home due to transportation reasons and remained in school. (Shanghai News Agency)

Classes Can Be Resumed on January 6

The annual holiday for schools in this city, according to the regulations of the Bureau of Education, is from New Year's Day for five days. This early holiday refers to the annual holiday. Reporters from Shanghai News Agency learned from the Bureau of Education yesterday that the Bureau of Education's notice was to advance the annual holiday by a few days. If the student movement can return to normal within these few days, then classes will resume as usual after the annual holiday, and the annual holiday will not be connected to the winter vacation. Classes can be resumed on January 6. As for the date of the winter vacation, it must be after January 2. Therefore, starting yesterday, all secondary schools have complied with the order. If any school fails to comply with the order and any accident occurs, the principal will be held responsible. (Shanghai News Agency)

Xi Yushu and Others Donate Food

Xi Yushu and others from the Fudan University Alumni Association purchased 200 yuan worth of food from Guanshengyuan, hired a car yesterday morning, and sent it to Suzhou to donate to Fudan students and persuade them to return to school.

Northern Station is Still Partially Under Martial Law

Military and police agencies worked all night in the police office at the North Station the night before last. At the same time, the area around the North Station was still heavily guarded by armed military and police. Barricades were set up on Kesonghai Road, Bingshan Road, and Zhejiang Road. The lights inside the station were dim. Except for the police, no pedestrians passed through. Since the suspension of trains at the North Station on the afternoon of the 23rd, passengers on the Beijing-Shanghai line have switched to taking buses on the Shanghai-Wuxi Highway. However, the Shanghai-Hangzhou line is still operating at the South Station and has not been interrupted. The Shanghai-Jiading commuter train and the Songhu branch line passenger trains are operating intermittently. Therefore, passengers feel deeply distressed. According to general statistics, the two railway bureaus have suffered losses of 300,000 yuan in passenger and freight transport. It is not yet possible to inspect and clarify whether there has been any damage to the trains.

University Faculty and Staff Association Issued Its Second Declaration Yesterday; The Nation Should Support the Patriotic Enthusiasm of Young People; Do Not Rashly Suppress Them Unless They Are Taking Advantage of the Situation to Cause Trouble 107

The Faculty and Staff Association of various universities in this city, being in a position to lead university students, cannot remain silent in the face of the current surging student unrest. It must express its views to guide the students towards the true path of national salvation. Therefore, after issuing a declaration on the current situation, it convened a meeting of executive and supervisory committee members a few days ago and immediately decided to issue another important declaration on the current situation. It clearly expressed its views on the national salvation steps for university professors and the attitude we should take towards the student movement. The general idea is that the nation should unanimously adhere to the following propositions: strictly rectify the diplomatic lineup, concentrate national strength to safeguard national sovereignty and territorial integrity, do not allow any special administrative organizations within the country that undermine unity to prevent disguised national treason by traitors, intellectual elites across the country, especially university professors, should fulfill their duties and quickly seek close organization and orderly steps to lead the people across the country and strive for effective national salvation work as a backing for the government to resist the enemy, the patriotic enthusiasm and movement of young students should be fully admired and assisted by all Chinese people, unless there are excesses that take advantage of the situation to cause trouble, the administrative authorities should not rashly suppress them to preserve the vitality of the Chinese nation.

Mayor Wu Hosted a Banquet for Leaders from All Circles Yesterday; He Reported on the Process of Discouraging Students; All Sectors Agreed That the Handling Was Appropriate 108

A Central News Agency report states that at noon yesterday, Mayor Wu invited leaders from all circles in Shanghai, such as Wang Xiaolai of the Municipal Council, Du Yuesheng and Qian Xinzhi of the Local Association, Yu Zuoting and Wang Yansong of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Chen Guangfu and Lin Kanghou of the Bankers' Association, Qin Runqing of the Money Industry Association, Li Zhaohuan and Liu Zhanen of the University Professors' Association, Baek Chi of the Newspaper Association, and Wu Kaixian of the Municipal Party Headquarters, totaling over ten people, to a lunch at the Municipal Government. After Mayor Wu briefly reported on the process of discouraging students the day before, all the attendees agreed that all the actions taken by the Municipal Government were appropriate and expressed their willingness to do their utmost to assist in maintaining local stability and order. The partial martial law declared in this city the day before has not yet been lifted.

All Students of Aurora University Aid Students in North China 109

An urgent message from all students of Aurora University: the Shanghai News and all newspapers nationwide are informed that the North China incident, in which a few traitors are using names and labels to damage national unity, have been strongly opposed by the Peiping and Tianjin students, while the local police have used force, which is outrageous. Aside from expressing their deepest sympathy to the students in North China, all our students ask the Central government to issue a formal declaration of war. We, as the backup, vow to stand up for the cause.

Zou Lu, Liu Luyin, and Others Returned South Together Yesterday Afternoon; Before Departing, They Said They Would Come North Again in About a Month; At That Time, Mr. Hu Hanmin May Travel to Beijing with Them 110

Zou Lu, a member of the Central Standing Committee, and Liu Luyin, the Minister of Propaganda of the Central Committee, along with Central Committee member Mai Huanzhang and Zou's secretary Cao Siwu, took the "President Grant" of the Da Lai Company at 1 PM yesterday, hurrying south. Deputy President of the Judicial Yuan Tan Zhen and many others went to the harbor to see them off. Before leaving, Zou said that he would come north again in about a month. At that time, Central Committee member Hu Hanmin might travel to Beijing with them. The details are as follows:

Returning South Together Zou arrived in Shanghai to wait for the ship and met with Liu Luyin and others. Yesterday, Liu decided to return south with Zou. Liu took the Da Lai ferry at 11:45 AM, while Zou took the Customs Jinghui special ferry at 12:10 PM, both from the new customs pier, crossing the Huangpu River to board the ship. The ship left Shanghai from the Da Lai wharf in Bailianjing, Pudong, at 1 PM. Those who went south on the same ship yesterday also included Central Committee member Mai Huanzhang. However, Central Committee member Hu Wencan stayed in Shanghai temporarily because, during the Fifth National Congress, it was decided that the Central Committee would allocate construction funds to Sun Yat-sen University and reimburse Guangdong for military expenses advanced during the Northern Expedition. Hu still needs to contact the Central Committee to achieve a result before returning south. Therefore, he will stay in Beijing and Shanghai for about a week.

Tan and Others See Off At that time, those who went to the pier to see them off included Vice President of the Judicial Yuan Tan Zhen, Superintendent of the Jianghai Customs Tang Haian, Central Committee member Hu Wencan, Commissioner Xie Cufu of the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission of the National Government, Wu Zhinan, the representative of the Shanghai Security Department Director Yang Hu, and Wang Zhisheng, Qian Chengju, Hu Xiyuan, Zhang Juansheng, and friends of Zou and Liu such as Wang Xiaoya, Zhang Mumin, and Huang Huabiao, totaling thirty people.

Zou's Speech Zou, before leaving at the new customs pier, gave a speech to the New Voice News reporter, saying that his return south was due to public and private matters such as school affairs at Zhongshan University in Guangzhou that needed to be handled. After passing through Hong Kong on this trip, he would transfer back to Guangdong. The rumor that he would go to Singapore to welcome Mr. Hu was not accurate. As for Mr. Hu's return to China, we had already set off after leaving France. I have not received confirmation. When Mr. Hu returns to China, he will, of course, pass through Hong Kong because of the shipping schedule. I plan to come north again in about a month, after the matter is settled. At that time, Mr. Hu can travel to Beijing with me.

Yunnan Sojourners Association in Shanghai Held Yunnan Uprising Memorial Meeting Yesterday and Held Sojourners Congress to Re-elect Executive and Supervisory Committee Members 111

Shanghai Times News Agency reports that yesterday was the 20th anniversary of Yunnan's support for the Republic. The Yunnan sojourners in Shanghai held a meeting at noon yesterday at the Youth Association on the 9th floor of Baxianqiao to commemorate the event and continued to hold the 6th Congress of all sojourners. Over one hundred people attended the meeting, chaired by Mr. Zhang Yaozeng. After the meeting started and the opening remarks were made, Mr. Yin Shuhuan, who participated in the revolution, reported on the military process of opposing the imperial system. His speech was roughly divided into three points: the relationship between the Yunnan Army and the National Revolution, the understanding of the fearless spirit of the National Protection Army, and the causes and consequences of the gains and losses of the Yunnan Army in the Chinese military status. The report was very detailed and the language was sincere. Lu Zian, the member of the Yunnan Provincial Government and director of the Finance Department, gave a speech, saying that he took the opportunity to attend the Fifth National Congress to pass through Shanghai and was able to participate in this grand meeting, which made him think about Yunnan's support for the Republic. The success of Yunnan's support for the Republic was purely due to the Yunnan leaders and the Yunnan people's recognition of justice and their love, not due to external agitation. Therefore, this glorious history must be fought for by Yunnan. Yunnan did not hesitate to sacrifice for national protection and the suffering it endured in order to win this great memorial should recognize the value of this memorial. The language was earnest and sincere. Li Liejun, a senior who participated in this revolution, also sent a telegram of congratulations, which read, "To the Yunnan sojourners in Shanghai, at this time of hardship, we should shake off our decline. Looking back, we cannot help but feel the vicissitudes. However, the great strategy of our predecessors and the noble spirit of Yunnan will surely shine through the ages. Respectfully, Li Liejun." Zhao Chengbo read an article about the memories of the Yunnan Uprising on behalf of Mr. Li Liejun. Zhu Gaoru, the brigade commander, then explained the spirit of the Yunnan Army carrying on the national protection, participating in the revolutionary Northern Expedition, and fighting against Japan in Shandong. After a joyful meal, at 2 PM in the afternoon, the 6th Yunnan Sojourners Congress was held to discuss many proposals. Then the executive and supervisory committee members were re-elected. Zhang Yaozeng, Song Chongjiu, Zhang Yongseng, and others received the most votes. The meeting adjourned happily at 5 PM.

Representatives from All Circles in Shanghai Hold Yunnan Uprising Commemoration Meeting; Over a Hundred People from the Party Headquarters Attend; Chairman Xing Wan Reports the Significance 112

December 25th is the anniversary of the Yunnan Uprising. The municipal party headquarters specially convened representatives from all circles on this day to hold a commemoration meeting. Chairman Xing Wan of the Municipal Committee reported the significance of the commemoration. The meeting adjourned without chanting slogans. The details of the commemoration meeting are recorded as follows:

Representatives Attending from All Circles

Those attending the commemoration meeting included: Xing Wan of the Municipal Committee, Wang Zongyan of the Jianghai Customs Superintendent's Office, Zhang Lichun of the Municipal Education Association, Lin Kecong of the Municipal Women's Association, Yu Zhenhui of the Municipal Farmers' Association, Sheng Yizhang of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' Shanghai Office, Jiang Shouchun of National Tongji University, Bao Jiasheng of the First District Paper Industry Association, Yu Yaoqiu of the Baoshan Fellow Villagers Association, and over a hundred people, including staff members from all levels of the party headquarters, various schools, and the entire staff of the municipal party headquarters, presided over by Chairman Xing Wan.

Chairman Reports the Significance

After performing the customary rites, Chairman Xing Wan delivered a report, stating roughly that today is the 21st anniversary of the Yunnan Uprising. On December 12th of the Republic of China's 4th year, Yuan Shikai issued an order to proclaim himself emperor, and the whole country, both the court and the public, rose up in opposition. The Yunnan comrades of our party took the lead in urging Tang Jiyao to express his opposition and telegraphed Yuan Shikai on the 23rd to demand a reply within a limited time. Yuan ignored it and acted wilfully. The generals of Yunnan, filled with righteous indignation, declared independence on the 25th, organized the National Protection Army, and set out for the provinces of Sichuan, Hunan, Guizhou, and Guangxi. Before long, comrades in various provinces responded one after another. Yuan also knew that the general trend was irreversible and that the will of the people could not be forced, and on March 22nd of the following year, he issued an order to abolish his imperial claim. From this, we can see that the revolutionary forces are sure to suppress all reactionary behaviors. Although the Yunnan Uprising was tens of thousands of miles away from the then Beijing government, the revolutionary forces spread one after another, and Yuan eventually ended up ruined and discredited. The Republic of China's achievements today are of infinite value, he said.

Slogans of the Commemoration Meeting

The Yunnan Uprising was a revolutionary movement to overthrow the imperial system, Commemorate the Yunnan Uprising to eradicate feudal forces, Commemorate the Yunnan Uprising to wipe out national humiliation, Complete the political tutelage construction, Eliminate the Red bandits, Long live the Three Principles of the People, Long live the Chinese Nationalist Party, Long live the Republic of China.

Yesterday was the 20th anniversary of the Yunnan Uprising. The special party branches of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways in this port held a commemoration meeting in the auditorium of the association. Over a hundred people attended, including representatives from the railway bureau, the first district party branch of the two railway labor unions, and various schools. Comrade Wang Cheng presided over the meeting. After leading the attendees in performing the rites, he reported on the revolutionary process of the Yunnan Uprising and the significance of the commemoration. Then, Comrade Li Guohua delivered a speech. Due to its length, it is not recorded here. The meeting then adjourned after chanting slogans.

The discussion ended at around 5:00 PM, and the meeting adjourned.

Water Patrol Team Handles Registration of Opium Smokers on the Huangpu River; Over 20,000 Households of Boats and Crews Make Declarations, Guaranteeing That There Are No Opium Smokers Among the Boatmen; If Opium Smokers Are Found, the Boat Owner Will Be Held Accountable 115

The Beijing-Shanghai, Tianjin-Pukou, and Longhai Railways Will Implement Shanghai West Through-Transport Wagon-Load Service Starting on New Year's Day; Agreed on Regulations for Handling at Each Location and Train Schedules; The Traffic Department Has Notified All Stations 116

The joint transportation service operated by the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Bureaus has been quite successful. Now, in consultation with the Tianjin-Pukou and Longhai Railways, it has been decided to operate through-transport wagon-load direct trains between Shanghai and Xi'an, starting on New Year's Day next year. The Traffic Department has been ordered to notify all stations. The detailed rules for handling have been approved by the ministry. The details are recorded as follows:

The through-transport wagon-load train will temporarily have two 40-ton covered wagons attached to each train. The Beijing-Shanghai Railway will dispatch eight wagons, the Tianjin-Pukou Railway will dispatch eight wagons, and the Longhai Railway will dispatch sixteen wagons, for a total of thirty-two wagons. These wagons will not be charged rent from each other and will not be included in the transshipment accounts. Each train should have one escort from each railway, and the vehicles of one road are escorted by one escort from one road. It is also stipulated that all wagon-load goods from each station between Beijing and Shanghai, arriving at the Longhai Railway via Xuzhou Station on the Tianjin-Pukou Railway, or from each station via the Longhai Railway, unless a whole wagon of wagon-load goods can be directly loaded to each of these railways, should all be loaded into these wagon-load trains. As for wagon-load goods arriving at each station of the Tianjin-Pukou Railway, they should be loaded into the Shanghai-Xuzhou or Shanghai-Beiping wagon-load trains. After the implementation of the Shanghai West wagon-load train, Xuzhou will no longer handle transshipments. All whole wagons of wagon-load goods arriving at Xuzhou from the Beijing-Shanghai Railway must not be combined with goods arriving at or via the Longhai Railway, so as to avoid confusion. When Beijing-Shanghai Longhai vehicles are damaged on the Tianjin-Pukou Railway, the Tianjin-Pukou Railway should dispatch vehicles to replace and reload the goods, and repair the damaged vehicle. Before the replacement vehicle returns to the original route of the damaged vehicle, it should be returned to the original route. After the original route receives the repaired empty vehicle, it should return the replacement vehicle to Tianjin-Pukou immediately after arriving at Xi'an or Shanghai. When Tianjin-Pukou vehicles are damaged on the Beijing-Shanghai or Longhai Railways, the respective railway should dispatch vehicles to replace them. After the damaged vehicle is repaired and the replacement vehicle returns to the location of the damaged vehicle (Xi'an or Shanghai), they will be exchanged. When Longhai vehicles are damaged on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway or Beijing-Shanghai vehicles are damaged on the Longhai Railway, they should be handled according to the second item.

Train Schedule: The operation of the through-transport wagon-load train and attached train is determined as follows: On the first day, Shanghai loads goods and attaches them to Beijing-Shanghai Train No. 502. It departs at 18:40. On the second day, the train arrives in Nanjing at 9:35. On the same day, it crosses the Yangtze River and spends the night in Pukou. On the third day, it attaches to Tianjin-Pukou Train No. 72 and departs at 7:10, arriving in Xuzhou at 19:00. On the fourth day, loading and unloading take place in Xuzhou. On the fifth day, it departs from Xuzhou attached to Longhai Train No. 10 at 1:08, arriving in Tongshan at 1:20. It departs from Tongshan attached to Train No. 111 at 3:45, arriving in Kaifeng at 18:00. From Kaifeng Station, it departs on Train No. 121 at 19:25, arriving in Zhengzhou at 22:40. On the sixth day, loading and unloading take place in Zhengzhou. On the seventh day, it departs from Zhengzhou attached to Train No. 121 at 0:10, arriving in Luoyang at 7:25. It departs from Luoyang attached to Train No. 130 at 9:05, arriving in Tongguan at 24:00. On the eighth day, it departs from Tongguan attached to Train No. 151 at 9:05, arriving in Xi'an at 16:15. On the ninth day, loading and unloading take place in Xi'an. On the tenth day, it departs from Xi'an attached to Train No. 152 at 4:15, arriving in Tongguan at 10:48. It departs from Tongguan attached to Train No. 132 at 22:30. On the eleventh day, Train No. 132 arrives at Luoyang East Station at 13:15. It departs from Luoyang East Station attached to Train No. 122 at 14:50, arriving in Zhengzhou at 22:30. On the twelfth day, loading and unloading take place in Zhengzhou. On the thirteenth day, it departs from Zhengzhou attached to Train No. 122 at 0:25, arriving in Kaifeng at 3:40. It departs from Kaifeng attached to Train No. 112 at 5:25, arriving in Tongshan at 19:10. It departs from Tongshan attached to Train No. 102 at 21:00, arriving in Xuzhou at 21:12. On the fourteenth day, it departs from Xuzhou attached to Train No. 71 at 7:50, arriving in Pukou at 20:15. On the fifteenth day, after crossing the Yangtze River from Nanjing, it attaches to Train No. 501 and departs at 18:40. On the sixteenth day, Train No. 501 arrives in Shanghai at 10:50 to unload goods. The seventeenth day is the same as the first day.

The Time Limit for Using Thin Ledger Stamps Ends on the General Closing Day; The National Federation of Commerce Received Approval from the Ministry of Finance 117

Lin Kanghou, chairman of the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce, for the time limit for businesses to exchange and use thin ledger stamps, has received approval from the Ministry of Finance, ending on the commercial general closing day. He specially sent a telegram to notify the provincial federations of commerce yesterday, to inform all chambers of commerce to comply. The original telegram said: All provincial federations of commerce across the country are informed. This association previously received a telegram from the Beiping Municipal Chamber of Commerce, requesting that the Ministry of Finance stipulate the time limit for exchanging and using stamps for ledgers, please forward to the Legislative and Judicial Yuan, and issue a general order to comply. This association forwarded a telegram to the Ministry of Finance, after which, on December 24th of this year, the Ministry of Finance issued approval No. 8205, which stated: I have read your telegram. This case was previously submitted by the Beiping Municipal Chamber of Commerce. I have already stated that "According to the regulations of the Stamp Tax Law, ledgers must be stamped with 2 jiao of stamps each year. The validity of the stamps should end at the end of December of the Gregorian calendar. However, because the exchange of ledgers in the commercial field is usually after the commercial general closing, the detailed rules for the implementation of the Stamp Tax Law have clearly stipulated in Article 10 that the validity of ledger stamps should end on the commercial general closing day, in order to show flexibility and facilitate matters. The request should not be discussed again," etc. I have received this approval. I should telegraph to your association accordingly, and I hope that you will investigate and inform the chambers of commerce in your province to comply with it. Lin Kanghou, Chairman of the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce.

Invoices Also Serving as Receipts Only Require One Type of Stamp 118

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce replied to the Petroleum Industry Association yesterday, instructing on the method of stamping invoices that also serve as receipts. The letter stated: In response, I received your letter of the 24th of this month. If the invoice only has one copy, after it is handed to the customer, it is still stamped by the customer as proof of receipt of the goods, and returned to the seller for inspection. When the seller issues the invoice, they have already affixed enough stamps according to the invoice tax rate. This means that one invoice is used as both an invoice and a receipt for goods. According to Article 8 of the Stamp Tax Law, if the same document has two or more properties, and the tax rates are the same, only one type of stamp should be affixed. Therefore, if this one document is stamped according to the invoice, even if it also serves as a receipt, there is no need to affix another stamp.

Amidst Drizzling Rain, West Bridge Celebrates Christmas; Christmas Scenes Fill the Streets; Dance Halls Rave Until Dawn; Church Bells Ring Loudly as Westerners Flock to Services 120

Yesterday was the Christmas Day holiday for Europeans and Americans. Western residents in Shanghai celebrated enthusiastically. All Western organizations, schools, institutions, and banks were closed. Starting last night, the Christian churches rang their bells loudly, and morning services were held. The dance halls were open all night, with singing and dancing until dawn. Although the wind and rain persisted from morning to noon, the enthusiasm did not diminish. The details are recorded as follows:

Santa Hats and Holly Fill the Streets

Western stores had already decorated with Santa Claus and snow scenes made of holly a few days before Christmas to attract business. Yesterday morning, all Western stores in the streets of the foreign concessions were filled with snow scenes and Santa Claus. The areas where foreigners were concentrated, such as Avenue Joffre, Nanjing Road, and Jing'an Temple Road, had even more Santa Claus figures and winter scenes. Even large stores established by Chinese merchants, such as Sincere, Wing On, and The Sun, also had festive Christmas displays in their shop windows, which were dazzling and spectacular.

Westerners Take Holidays, Churches Hold Services

Westerners from all organizations, schools, institutions, and banks took holidays. They also participated in Christmas services yesterday morning. Because Christmas is one of the four major holidays of the Catholic Church, the churches also held solemn services. At midnight last night, more than twenty Catholic churches in the city held midnight mass, and the bells rang in unison, which could be heard clearly. Believers all went to participate. In the morning, there was still a mass, with scripture readings and singing, which was very solemn and enthusiastic. Its grandeur was rare.

Dance Halls and Singing Continue All Night

Because all places were closed yesterday, the number of tourists at the entertainment venues, cinemas, and amusement parks in the city increased sharply, and business was booming. The dance halls were also specially approved by the Municipal Council to operate all night and gave Christmas gifts to dancers, such as balloons and Santa hats. On the night of the 24th, the dance halls were already full, with fragrant clothes, glittering hairpins, and intertwined skirts. Singing and dancing made people feel like they were in paradise, almost believing that it was a time of peace and prosperity, forgetting that they were in a period of national crisis.

Major Fire at Dunlop Warehouse; Fire Started on the Fifth Floor and Spread to the Third Floor; The Second Floor and Ground Floor Were Also Half Destroyed 122

Total Losses Estimated at 600,000 Yuan

The warehouse of the British Dunlop Rubber Tire Company, located at No. 89 Fuzhou Road, had a total of five floors. The ground floor was used by Dunlop to store tires and manufacturing materials. The second floor was rented by the Hengmao Transfer Company to store various warehoused goods. The third floor was rented by the Gongli Foreign Firm, Yizhong Mark, and F茂 Foreign Firm to store electrical materials and leather goods. The fourth and fifth floors were rented by Yifeng Changhao to store silk and cotton. The day before yesterday and yesterday were the Western Christmas holiday, so all office and warehouse staff in the warehouse were on vacation and out. It was not until the evening that they returned to the warehouse to rest. Unexpectedly, at about 3:30 AM yesterday morning, when the staff were sound asleep, a fire suddenly broke out in the pile of silk and cotton on the fifth floor of the Yifeng Changhao. Because no one noticed it at the time, it was allowed to spread. By the time the fire broke through the roof and was spotted by passers-by and patrolling police, who knocked on the door on the ground floor to call for help, it was too late to save it. The flames soared into the sky, and the red light shone everywhere. Moreover, the fifth floor was extremely high, and it was impossible to save it urgently. The fire department was immediately called to dispatch all fire trucks to rush to the scene to put out the fire. Some firefighters tried to go up from below, but the fourth and third floors had already been affected, and the thick smoke caused people to faint. Moreover, the warehouse doors were all locked, so it was impossible to know what the internal fire situation was like. There was no way to enter, so they changed their method, erected ladders, and watered from above and below. At the same time, they took defensive measures around the warehouse to prevent it from spreading. All the fire hydrants in the nearby area were connected with hoses, crisscrossing the ground, and water accumulated on the roads, forming small canals, and traffic was completely blocked. Looking back at the fire in the warehouse, it was still increasing. The flames were visible from the roof, like a hot pot. The fierceness of the burning was evident. At this time, the firefighters spared no effort to fight the fire bravely. After more than four hours of continuous watering, the fire was slightly reduced, but the embers were not exhausted, and it still flared up here and there. It was not until about 10:00 AM that the fire was completely extinguished. As a result, the third, fourth, and fifth floors were completely destroyed, and the second floor and the ground floor were also half burned. The total loss was as high as 600,000 yuan. However, the various firms in the warehouse had fire insurance. As for the cause of the fire, it is difficult to determine for a while. The police are investigating.

At 2:30 PM on December 23rd, Xu Jujin, a cashier from the accounting office of the Railway Bureau, was dispatched to carry more than 4,200 yuan in cash and more than 2,200 yuan in bank checks to the engineering office to pay the December salaries. The Tragic Qian Family Murder in West Shanghai: Robbery and Murder Claim the Lives of Father and Son; Zhu Afu Confesses to Multiple Accomplices 125

In West Shanghai, at number 13 Ganjiazhai, Chenjiadu, north of Zhoujiaqiao Creek, resided Gan A'er, a 35-year-old native of Shanghai who made a living by farming. At around 6 PM last night, four robbers suddenly arrived. Two were armed with handguns and broke down the door. The Gan family was terrified and dared not make a sound. They were robbed of six silver dollars and twenty or thirty pieces of cloth and clothing. As the robbers, each with their loot, were about to leave, Qian Jinquan, a 21-year-old Shanghai resident living at number 7 next door, caught a glimpse of them and shouted "Catch the thieves!" at the door. In their desperation, the robbers fired several shots, two of which hit Qian in the abdomen and next to his left breast, piercing his intestines and internal organs. He immediately collapsed to the ground, bleeding profusely, and died on the spot. Seeing the enormity of their crime, the robbers immediately fled north, passing through Chenjiazhai, the northern Xin Cemetery, and behind the Zhang Family Ancestral Hall. There, they encountered the deceased's father, Qian Amao, 43 years old, who was returning from his work at the Zhaofeng Garden. Seeing the robbers with guns coming from the direction of Ganjiazhai, he suspected they were robbers and shouted "Robbers!" In the chaos of their escape, the robbers immediately turned and fired, hitting Qian in the chest. He immediately fell into a pool of blood. At that time, members of the Second Team of the Pusong District Defense Corps were patrolling and heard the gunshots. They immediately searched in all directions and captured one of the escaping robbers, Zhu Afu, near the Zhang Family Ancestral Hall. Meanwhile, the injured Qian Amao was transported by car to the Red Cross Hospital on Haige Road, but he died of his injuries before reaching the hospital. According to the captured robber Zhu Afu, 22 years old and a native of Huzhou, he and his accomplices Zhou Rongqing (aka Wang Dexiu), Wu Aliul, and Ying Gongqing, etc., lived together at number 12 Chongde Lane, Weihaiwei Road. He confessed that on the 24th at around 5 PM, they gathered at a certain beef restaurant next to the Hongfei Theater in Wujiaochang, Caojiadu, and conspired to commit robbery in Chenjiadu. The team immediately sent the captured robber Zhu Afu to the Caojiadu Public Security Bureau. The detective team leader Liang Yu, Huang Zhonghe, squad leaders Liu Bingyuan and Liu Shaoqing, and detectives Zhang Zuoxian and Zhang Diling, together with the concession police, searched the address but found nothing. They also went to number 11 Wuxing Lane, Malang Road, and arrested a suspected female offender, Wu, 22 years old, who stated she used to work as a maid. Her husband's name was Zhou Rongqing, who also used to work but was now unemployed and she did not know what he was doing outside. She said that a friend of her husband had come to visit and they had gone out together but had not yet returned. The team is currently strictly searching for the escaping robbers. Meanwhile, the local Bao Zhang has reported the case to the Shanghai Local Court to inspect the bodies of Qian Amao and Qian Jinquan, father and son, who were robbed and murdered.

Gods and Buddhas, Puppets All in One Place: Second Sister Treats Illnesses and Collects Money, Actually Claiming Three Gods Take Turns Possessing Her and Displaying Miraculous Powers; Superstitious Women Are Bewildered and Deceived Out of a Lot of Money 127

—Zhang Chengda Discovers the Secret and Files a Lawsuit—

Zhu Guangbu, a native of Wuxi, is 27 years old, and his wife, Zhou Suyang, also known as Second Sister, is 32 years old. They live together at number 1308, Liuhe Lane, Roberts Road in West Shanghai. Their home has a shrine with statues of gods and Buddhas, arranged in a very imposing fashion. All the deities commonly worshipped, such as Guanyin, Jigong, and Lu Zu, are displayed. In addition, there are the so-called Grand Mother, Second Father, and Third Lord, three evil gods summoned from Shangfang, Suzhou, who specialize in treating illnesses. Second Sister is skilled in socializing,

and her footprints can be found in the homes of officials, gentry, and wealthy people. Thus, she is able to take the opportunity to wag her tongue and make exaggerated claims, declaring that these three gods take turns possessing her every evening, each displaying miraculous powers. This woman is not only eloquent but also proficient in various local dialects. When she speaks with a soft Wu accent, she claims to be possessed by the "Grand Mother." Then she switches to Mandarin, saying that "Third Lord" has arrived. Finally, she changes to a stuttering tone, indicating that "Second Father" has descended. Ordinary superstitious women are all bewitched by the appearances of these demons and monsters, and flock to her home to pray, or

beg for divine healing. Zhu and Zhou respond according to the individual, either giving them talismans to suppress evil spirits, or providing incense ash to be used as a remedy. If the patient does not improve after taking it, they blame the person for not being sincere. If a patient suddenly recovers, they boast of their god's omnipotence. Therefore, since the establishment of the incense hall, countless people have been fooled and deceived out of money, and Zhu's pockets have been filled daily. This summer, a fellow villager named Zhang Chengda, whose child was ill, was misled by rumors and also went to Zhu's home to seek divine treatment. At first,

the expenses were minimal. After several visits, Second Sister became familiar with the Zhang couple, and their interactions became increasingly intimate. Later, she realized that Zhang was gullible and began to use manipulative tricks. Whenever she went to Zhang's home, she would say that his residence was unlucky, his wife was jinxed, and his son had heavy evil influences. If he did not seek a remedy urgently, there was a risk of death. Zhang, wanting to protect the lives of his wife and children, reluctantly sacrificed money. There were six instances where he was cheated out of one hundred and ten dollars each, and another five hundred and six dollars. However,

Zhu and his wife were still not satisfied with their greed. They claimed that the incense hall was too small and needed to be expanded, and asked Zhang to donate money. Zhang, who was originally a sample maker, agreed to draw construction plans and undertake the painting work after the incense hall was completed. The amount of money he helped with, whether it was for incense or to buy silver ingots, was even harder to count. It was not until recently that Zhang discovered the inside story of Zhu and Second Sister using gods and Buddhas to defraud people. He believed that if he continued to endure this, the harm would be endless, so he hired a lawyer and filed a

criminal self-accusation of fraud and intimidation against Zhu Guangbu and Second Sister in the First Special District Local Court. The day before yesterday afternoon, Judge Jiang opened the court to summon and interrogate them. The defendant, Second Sister, was dressed in splendid clothes, looking like a noblewoman, while Zhu Guangbu argued that his family worshipped Buddha and respected gods, which was true, but they did not use it to collect money. He also claimed that he had a considerable amount of property, and that he had disagreements with the plaintiff because of stock market transactions, and that he was now being falsely accused out of spite. He also hired three lawyers to represent him. After the court finished questioning, it announced that the verdict would be announced next Monday afternoon.

(The spot was about two hundred paces from the No. 14 post). At the time, the weather was rainy and the light was dim, with few pedestrians, so no one had noticed. Later, Zhang Hongji, a resident of number 277 Xietu Road, caught a glimpse of it and reported it to the police on duty at the post, who in turn reported it to the Ximen Public Security Bureau. Notice to the Pawn Industry: Shorten the Pawn Period, Effective on New Year's Day; Goods Pawned Before Will Still Be Handled According to Previous Regulations 131

In order to help fellow businesses, the Shanghai pawn industry has shortened the pawn period from eighteen months to twelve months. After being approved by the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, and after a joint meeting of new and old colleagues, it was decided to implement it on New Year's Day next year. The industry association issued an urgent notice yesterday, stating, "In recent years, the market has been depressed and prices have fallen. The styles of men's and women's clothing have changed from time to time, resulting in a sharp decline in the redemption of goods pawned by colleagues. The sales at the end of the period have suffered heavy losses. In response to the request of colleagues, this association has applied to the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau and has been approved to shorten the pawn period from eighteen months to twelve months in order to provide relief. It has been decided by a joint meeting of new and old colleagues convened by this association to implement the shortened period for colleagues starting from January 1, 25th year of the Republic. All goods pawned before will still be handled according to previous regulations. In addition to reporting, this announcement is published in the newspaper to inform you."

Hangzhou: Scheduled Memorial Service for Zhu Yaoyan 134

Zhu Yaoting, the Director of the Zhejiang Provincial Highway Administration, has served as the Director of the Hangzhou Municipal Engineering Bureau, the Director of the Navigation Administration Bureau of the Ministry of Communications, and other positions. He was honest and selfless, and worked diligently. Since being transferred to the Zhejiang Provincial Highway Administration in February of the 23rd year of the Republic, he actively worked with Director Zeng of the Zhejiang Construction Department to complete the province's highway network. He supervised the design and worked day and night. He also spared no effort to plan the operation of the completed roads, and was greatly relied upon by the construction authorities. At 4:00 PM on the 28th of last month, Zhu went to the Zhejiang Construction Department to meet with Wang Guohua, the secretary of the department and the director of the purchasing committee, to discuss the purchase of automobile materials and the use of charcoal vehicles. He then felt slightly unwell and returned to his residence to rest. Unexpectedly, his condition worsened rapidly within half an hour and he passed away. According to doctors, it must have been due to excessive work on weekdays and severe heart damage, which led to this disease. Therefore, Zhu's friends and construction colleagues were all deeply saddened. In addition to the coffin being returned to his ancestral home in Haiyan on the 8th of this month, friends and construction colleagues in Hangzhou believe that Zhu has been serving in the engineering field since returning to China from the United States. He was honest and selfless throughout his life and loyal to his duties. During his tenure at the Zhejiang Provincial Highway Administration, he completed 2,000 kilometers of highways in less than two years. His perseverance and sense of responsibility are admirable. Director Zeng initiated the organization of a memorial service preparation office in the Provincial Highway Administration, and many decisions were made at the preparation meeting held in the Zhejiang Construction Department. It is now known that the date of the memorial service has been set for 8:00 AM on the 29th of this month (Sunday) at the Hangzhou West Lake Auditorium. People from all walks of life in Beijing, Shanghai, and Hangzhou who have friendships with Zhu will attend. It is conceivable that at that time, the plain cars and white horses in front of the auditorium will be a lively scene. It is heard that the date of Zhu's funeral帖 will be determined separately by the family and announced.

Jianghai Customs Notice: Sodium Chloride Prohibited from Import 135

Tang Haian, the Customs Superintendent of the Jianghai Customs, and Baron Sen, the Tax Commissioner, yesterday issued Notice No. 1489, jointly signed, to announce the amendment to the ban on the import of coloring materials and other chemicals containing more than 20% chlorine, stating, "It has been found that the import of sodium chloride (i.e., table salt) has been banned. It has been stipulated that all coloring materials and other chemicals containing more than 20% sodium chloride are prohibited from import. This has been announced in Notice No. 1383 on August 28, 23rd year of the Republic. Now, according to the order of the Ministry of Finance, the aforementioned ban has been amended as follows: 'Coloring materials and other chemicals containing more than 20% sodium chloride are prohibited from import, but those for scientific experiments and medical purposes may be transported by the reporter in accordance with the Sodium Chloride Ban Regulations, and apply to the salt affairs authority in each province for a sodium chloride transport license from the Ministry of Finance for reporting and transportation. Each batch is limited to 200 market pounds of net weight of sodium chloride. The weight of other components contained in the goods shall be deducted for calculation. The reporter shall find out the amount of sodium chloride contained in the goods and report it to the salt affairs authority in the province for filling in the license. After the goods arrive at the customs, the customs will verify the quantity of sodium chloride limited on the license and levy taxes for release.' etc. Therefore, compliance should be followed. All merchants should be aware of this and a special announcement is made."

Appeal of the Police Department after the Russian Partner Was Murdered: In View of the Western Newspaper Commentary 139

The owner of the Russian bakery and confectionery store opened by a Russian, Beli Qiqiang (transliteration), 48 years old, at number 234-236, Albert Road in the French Concession, because his hired Russian partner, Seyi Mianuofu (transliteration), had indecent behavior towards his two daughters, Lala (transliteration), 9 years old, and Weiliang (transliteration), 6 years old. After Beli found out, he called Seyi upstairs in the store to reprimand him at 2:00 PM on the 26th of last month. Seyi did not realize his mistake, but instead tried to push and shove. Beli could not contain his anger for a moment, and stabbed Seyi to death with a beef knife. Afterwards, Beli surrendered to the French Police Station. After investigation by the French Police Department, he was sent to the Second Special Court and prosecuted for murder. After the trial was concluded, he was sentenced to twelve years of imprisonment for murder on the 7th of this month, as reported in the previous newspaper. It is now heard that the Police Department, in view of the comments written by various Western newspapers in Shanghai, mostly believed that the defendant Beli Qiqiang's murder was due to a momentary stimulus of anger, and it was unfair to be sentenced to a heavy penalty, and that the deceased's behavior was beyond the norm. Therefore, the Police Department specially filed an appeal with the Third Branch Court, hoping to reduce the defendant Beli Qiqiang's imprisonment.

Misappropriation of Private Accounts: Manager Beats the Bookkeeper 140

Hu Bingwen, a native of Huzhou, 24 years old, worked as a bookkeeper in the Zhenyuan Dyeing Workshop at the intersection of Pingliang Road and Fenzhou Road. The manager of the workshop was Zhu Wenyao, a native of Shaoxing, Zhejiang. Zhu previously discovered that Hu Bingwen had misappropriated an account among the accounts to be closed. Therefore, he repeatedly demanded it from him. However, Hu said that he was financially strapped and temporarily borrowed it, and did not intentionally misappropriate the customer's account. He begged the manager to be lenient and allow him to return it later. However, Zhu Wenyao firmly refused and repeatedly pressured him. Yesterday, the two sides had another quarrel over this matter. Zhu Wenyao became angry and punched Hu, causing Hu to be injured in the face and waist, and he fell to the ground. At that time, Zhu Wenyao saw that he had caused trouble and had a sudden idea. He first went to the Yulin Road Police Station, which had jurisdiction over the area, and reported that Hu Bingwen had misappropriated the account and committed embezzlement, and asked for his arrest. After the police station sent detectives to investigate, they saw Hu injured and lying on the ground. After questioning, they learned that he had been beaten by Zhu. Therefore, they sent Hu to the hospital for examination and then interrogated him again.

How Did Bullets End Up on a Rickshaw? 148

Liang Yu, the captain of the Detective Squad of the Caojiadu Public Security Bureau, along with Deputy Captain Huang Zhonghe, supervised team leaders Liu Bingyuan and Liu Shaoqing, detectives Su Ruiting, and police officer Shi Xiaosheng, among others. While patrolling outside yesterday at approximately 9:00 AM, they were in front of the Tiger Stove at the North Caojia Residence when they noticed a rickshaw puller acting suspiciously. They immediately searched the rickshaw and discovered dozens of bullets inside the carriage. The rickshaw puller was arrested. He stated that his name was Cao Yuanbi, 23 years old, from Taizhou, and he lived in a thatched shed at 128 Songjia Residence in Binbei. He claimed that the bullets were left in the rickshaw by a passenger. The rickshaw puller was taken back to the branch bureau and detained pending investigation.

Chen Amao Dies from Electric Shock 149

Chen Amao from Baoshan, 36 years old, lived near Tan Jia Bridge in Zhabei and made a living on a small scale. He had no wife and lived with his brother, who suffered from paralysis. Yesterday morning at 4:45 AM, Chen Amao went outside to use the toilet and was unaware that the power line there had been broken by the wind. Chen Amao did not notice and was electrocuted to death. Yesterday, the local security officer, Tan Yushan, reported the incident to the court, which sent personnel to verify the death and prepare for burial.

2. Maoxin Flour Mill - This factory is divided into factories 1, 2, 3, and 4. The first three factories are located in Wuxi, while the last factory is located in Jinan. The head office is located at 421 Jiangxi Road, Shanghai. All are operated by Rong Zongjing and are unlimited liability companies with a total capital of 1.45 million yuan. The equipment of each factory is listed below: (A) Factories 1 and 3 have a total of 36 flour machines, 1,200 horsepower of prime mover, a base covering 20 mu, and worker dormitories built outside the factory, with approximately 250 workers. (B) Factory 2 has 24 flour machines, 750 horsepower of prime mover, and more than 170 workers. (C) Factory 4 has 12 flour machines, 450 horsepower of prime mover, and a factory base covering 16 mu. Statistics show that the four factories produce 1.2 million bags of flour annually. The sales market is widest in Tianjin domestically, and there are also sales in Southeast Asia. Last year's profit was 280,000 yuan.

3. Fuxin Flour Mill - This factory is divided into eight factories. Factory 4 was closed four years ago, and Factory 5, located in Hankou, is also currently closed. The establishment year, address, capital, and other items of factories 1, 2, 3, 6, 7, and 8 are listed below:

The Fuxin factories are also operated by Rong Zongjing, and the Wang Yuqing and Wang Yaochen brothers are also major shareholders. It is an important town in China's flour industry, and the amount of its output is closely related to the market. The factory's products originally had the brands Baoxing, Fushou, and Fisherman, etc. Later, because their sales were not as smooth as "Warship", they were all changed to "Warship". The sales market is mainly in Tianjin, along the Yangtze River, coastal provinces, and Southeast Asia, and there are also large sales volumes. In the past, when the factory's business was booming, it could sell more than 20 million bags of flour annually. In recent years, due to the impact of the loss of the Northeast, the average has been reduced to about 17 million bags. Last year, the price of flour rose slightly, and the profit was greater. For example, the profits of factories 1, 3, 6, and 7 reached 1.5 million yuan. During nine days this year, Fuxin Factory 1 and other branch factories temporarily stopped work for about a month due to the lack of raw materials because inland wheat could not be continuously transported. It was not until the previous month that work was resumed.

In addition to Fufeng and Fuxin, there are also many flour mills in this city, such as Lida on Efeisi Road and Shenda on Jichang Street in Nanshi, but because they are smaller in scale, they will not be discussed here.

General Situation of the Flour Industry in Shanghai (Continued) (Part 7 of the General Situation of Industry and Commerce in Shanghai) 153

— Edited by China Credit Institute

3. Raw Materials for the Flour Industry - Wheat

The raw material for the flour industry is wheat. The main wheat-producing areas in my country are in the Yellow River provinces. In recent years, due to the invasion of natural disasters and man-made disasters, the amount of harvest has been greatly reduced. According to the survey by the Central Agricultural Experiment Institute, the national wheat production was 41,112,000 dan in the 21st year, 39,620,000 dan in the 22nd year, and 43,518,000 dan in the 23rd year. Although last year was slightly higher than in the previous two years, it still only accounted for 68% of the full harvest year. My country is originally an agricultural country, and according to the wheat harvest alone, there is no need to rely on foreign countries. However, flour factories in Shanghai sometimes also have to purchase foreign wheat, which is because domestic production is insufficient. In addition, inconvenient domestic transportation and the inability of wheat from distant places to arrive in Shanghai in time are also a major reason. According to customs statistics, since the 12th year of the Republic of China, wheat has been in deficit every year. The deficit numbers for the past three years and the first three quarters of this year are listed below for reference: (Unit: Customs Gold)

National Shanghai Port

Year 21 41,543,135 31,226,816

Year 22 45,062,543 35,942,749

Year 23 15,659,026 14,013,722

First three quarters of this year 17,025,245 Not detailed

The countries importing wheat are mostly the United States, followed by Canada and Australia. However, because the imported price of this kind of imported wheat is sometimes more expensive, it is not very cost-effective for Shanghai factories to purchase it for flour production. Therefore, whenever there is a domestic shortfall and transportation is not profitable, Shanghai factories still cannot avoid the pain of stopping work. According to a certain newspaper on September 25 of this year, Fuxin Factory 1 stopped manufacturing due to the reduced source of inland wheat and the lack of raw materials. Other factories such as Fuxin Factory 8 and Lida were also at risk of stopping work at that time. However, once ethnic flour manufacturers stop work, the opportunity for imported flour to enter will inevitably increase even more, which is something that we should pay attention to.

The flour-producing ability of wheat varies according to its type. Generally speaking, American wheat can produce 767 catties of flour and 22 catties of bran per 100 catties of raw wheat, white wheat can produce 745 catties of flour and 22 catties of bran, and Australian red wheat can produce 756 catties of flour and 23 catties of bran. The wheat produced in this country is of poor quality, and each 100 catties can only produce 70 catties of flour and 234 catties of bran. Bran, the by-product of the flour milling industry, was only used to feed livestock in the past, and its sales were limited to Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces. Recently, the Japanese have made good use of it to make gluten and seasoning foods, increasing its utility and gradually widening its sales, but it is still mostly purchased by the Japanese.

American wheat is divided into white-skinned and purple-skinned types, while Australian wheat is red-skinned, and domestic wheat is yellow-skinned, and their qualities also vary. White-skinned wheat is loose in texture and thin in skin, and the flour produced is clean and white, but lacks gluten. Purple-skinned wheat is solid and small, the flour color is slightly inferior, but the gluten is stronger. Red-skinned wheat is solid and thick-skinned, and the flour color is the same as that of purple-skinned wheat. Yellow-skinned wheat is solid and small, the flour produced is shiny and not inferior to the purple and red types, and the gluten is the strongest, accounting for about 40-50%, while other American, Australian and Cambodian wheat only accounts for about 40%. As for the impurities contained, the red and purple types have the least, about 2 catties, the white wheat is the next, about 4 catties, and the domestic wheat is the most mixed, up to 6 catties. This is the biggest shortcoming of domestic wheat. If we can find a way to improve it in the future, then the raw materials for flour production can be self-sufficient.

4. Rise and fall of wheat prices and flour prices

In recent years, wheat and flour prices in Shanghai have fluctuated from time to time. Wheat prices were slightly higher in the 21st year, lower in the 22nd year, and slightly rebounded last year. The first few months of this year were not much different from the second half of last year, but the upward trend was more intense after the implementation of the new currency policy. The rise and fall of flour prices are generally consistent with wheat, and there is no obvious distance between yarn and flowers. The following table is based on the statistics listed in the monthly Central Bank Monthly to facilitate the search:

In addition, the European Italian and Afghan situation is very tense, and no country has exports. Therefore, the price of flour in our country is rising step by step. The factory I operate will be completely closed by the end of this month due to lack of raw materials. Flour is an indispensable food for the people, and such a high price is a trivial matter for the national livelihood.

Children's Education Novel

Little Men (1)(3)(5) 159

— Original by Louisa M. Alcott, Translated by Zheng Xiaocang

They started off really well, but after an hour they gradually became bored and impatient with being confined indoors, and longed to be able to run outside. They heard the sounds from the main hall and wondered how interesting it must be there. Even the small bedroom held appeal; if they could imagine the curtains as military tents, there would be plenty to play with. The open window directly enticed them, because they couldn't go to the window to look out. The world outside felt so beautiful, and they privately thought, how could anyone say it was boring? Nan yearned to run a lap around the lawn. Rob suddenly remembered that he hadn't fed the dog that day, and wondered how poor Pluto was doing. They watched the clock, Nan dividing the hours into minutes, meticulously. Rob practiced telling time, from eight o'clock to one o'clock; he would never forget it. It was truly difficult, smelling the aroma of the food and knowing there was pearl rice with lentils, as well as blackberry pudding, yet they couldn't go to the table to eat their fill. When the maid, Annie, went to arrange the dishes, they wished they could transform themselves to see what meats there were. Poon even offered to help her make the beds if she would put extra sauce on her pudding.

When the students came out after their lessons, they saw the two children wrestling with the riding tack, like a pair of restless little ponies. They saw the results of last night's adventure and not only found it amusing but also learned quite a few lessons.

Wartime Education Work Plan

By the Colleagues of the Education Research Institute of Sun Yat-sen University

I. Wartime Work Plan for Educational Administration, II. Wartime Work Plan for Universities, III. Wartime Work Plan for High Schools, IV. Wartime Work Plan for Junior High Schools, V. Wartime Work Plan for Elementary Schools, VI. Wartime Work Plan for Civic Schools,

I. Wartime Work Plan for Educational Administration

A. Basic Principles: 1. Wartime work organization should be able to take care of both vertical and horizontal aspects. Vertically, the work at all levels—national, provincial, county, city, township, and school—should correspond with each other. Horizontally, the activities among educational administrative organs and schools, among schools, and among classes in the same area should be coordinated with each other. 2. All practical wartime activities should have strict procedures, that is, recognizing needs, then implementing training. Work must be carried out after training.

3. All faculty, staff, students, and workers of each school should participate. In addition to general work, each should focus on certain types of training according to their abilities, to achieve the effect of division of labor and cooperation. After receiving training themselves, they should also teach others.

4. Wartime education work should strive for centralized authority internally and cooperation externally.

B. Organizational System: 1. In order to ensure that the wartime work organization can take care of both vertical and horizontal aspects, each province, county, and city nationwide should establish a central agency as the hub of wartime education work, without the need for various small organizations. During periods of military emergency, all educational personnel in the province must be under the command of the provincial central agency. 2. The wartime work organization for education in the province will have the Provincial Wartime Education Work Committee as the highest authority, the County/City Wartime Education Work Committee as the central organization, and the School Wartime Work Committee as the basic organization.

3. The Provincial Wartime Education Work Committee shall be jointly organized by the Provincial Department of Education, the County/City Education Bureau (or Section), universities, middle schools, and public education centers. It shall consist of fifteen members, with the Director of the Provincial Department of Education and the President of the National University as ex-officio members. Other members shall be appointed from university presidents, experts, and designated County/City Education Bureau Directors (or Section Chiefs), middle and elementary school principals, and directors of provincial public education centers.

4. The County/City Wartime Education Work Committee shall be jointly organized by the County/City Education Bureau (or Section), middle and elementary schools, public education centers, and civic schools. It shall consist of nine members, with the County/City Education Bureau Director (or Section Chief) and the Principal of the Provincial Middle School as ex-officio members. Other members shall be appointed from experts and other middle school principals, and designated elementary school principals, public education center directors, and civic school principals.

5. The regulations for middle schools also apply to normal schools and vocational schools. 6. The Provincial Committee is a parallel agency to the Provincial Department of Education and universities, and the County/City Committee is a parallel agency to the local Education Bureau (or Section).

7. The organizational chart for each level is as follows:

8. The following departments shall be established under the Provincial/County (City) Wartime Work Committees: Personnel Registration Department, Needs Investigation Department, Skills Training Department, Curriculum Guidance Department, Social Work Department.

9. The task of the Personnel Registration Department is to register various technical talents and untrained personnel, and it shall have sections for military personnel, medical personnel, agricultural personnel, industrial personnel, and general personnel.

10. The task of the Needs Investigation Department is to manage the investigation of wartime needs in various aspects, and it shall have sections for population survey, occupational survey, food survey, daily necessities survey, military raw materials survey, and transportation survey.

11. The task of the Skills Training Department is to manage the training of various personnel during wartime, and it shall have sections for military training, scouting training, first aid training, defense training, fire fighting training, military supplies manufacturing, transportation engineering, and food production increase. 12. The task of the Curriculum Guidance Department is to plan and guide the progress of schoolwork during wartime, and it shall have sections for literature, history and geography, science, agriculture, and industry.

13. The task of the Social Work Department is to convey the wartime knowledge and skills obtained by the committee to the public and to manage matters related to the public. It shall have sections for publicity, introduction, fundraising, relief, and consolation. (To be continued)

Sports News

The Impact of the 1935-36 Basketball Rules on Basketball Training (Continued) 160

— Authored by Ruby of the United States, Translated by Qian Yiqin

The third diagram shows another famous offensive method, which has become ineffective due to the implementation of the new three-second rule. Number 4 passes to Number 1, Number 1 passes back to Number 4, Number 4 passes to Number 2, and Number 1 passes back to Number 4. Number 4 feints a drive and a long shot each time he advances, but according to this new rule, Number 1 only has time to receive the ball and pass it to Number 4 once.

Many teams have switched to the double pivot offense, especially when a team has one tall player and three short, agile players who are good at long shots. The fourth diagram shows a double pivot offense. This formation can be varied in several ways. This type of offense avoids violating the one-second rule. However, since there are only three players attacking in the front, the defense against players far from the ball can be slightly relaxed, as shown by the movement of players CA in Figure 4.

In the western Midwest of the United States, there is a trend toward the offensive formation shown in Figure 5. Because the area in front of the basket is open, players can break into that area to shoot, thereby allowing a team to avoid violating the two-second rule. The two points of many zone defenses are within the free throw area. The adoption of zone defenses will inevitably be more common than in the past. This is a natural trend, no doubt.

Due to requests from several parties, the National Basketball Rules Committee has partially approved the requests in the Pacific coastal area and has eliminated the center jump. The original text is as follows: "After a free throw is made due to a personal foul, the ball must be thrown in by the team that was fouled from any point outside the end line of the court. When the ball is thrown into the court, the time is restarted. At this time, the referee does not need to take the ball and hand it over." (Note 3)

The implementation of this rule will likely eliminate 5,000 percent of the previous center jump. Therefore, coaches cannot spend as much time as they used to practicing center court offensive formations, but will instead use that time to train how to quickly attack after a free throw is made due to a personal foul. Suppose after Team A makes a free throw due to a personal foul, Team B's guard or center quickly holds the ball and stands outside the end line of the court and throws it to his teammate's forward for a quick counterattack. This counterattack may or may not achieve special results, but at least it can cause Team A's players to quickly retreat to defense out of concern, so that they have less chance of getting the ball when their shot is missed.

Team B's quick counterattack can be delayed by Team A retrieving the ball after the free throw is made. How much this delay will be is unknown until the official new rules are released this season. However, according to situation 298 in the book "The Scenarios of the Basketball Game," "After Team A's number 1 completes the free throw, the ball is awarded to Team B to throw in from the end line. However, because Team A wants enough time to form its defensive formation, Team A's number 1 hits the ball under the seat. Rule—The referee has the right to declare a technical foul for unsportsmanlike conduct."

(Chapter 15, Article 1, Example 4)

Over the years, many coaches have felt that when a player is fouled during a legitimate shot, the player should have the right to refuse the penalty. However, such a rule would be extremely difficult to implement. The rules for 1935-36 clearly state that such shots should be counted. However, from the moment of the foul until the shot is made, the shooter's movement must be continuous. If he makes any new movement after the whistle, the shot will not be counted. Therefore, from the coach's point of view, this change will change the tactics of the game.

One of the smartest changes in the new rules is that "dribbling a ball that is not stable and dribbling it continuously shall not be considered dribbling," and "When a player taps the ball in the air once or several times to prevent other players from contesting it, the dribbling action shall not be considered to have started." In the past, because of this old rule, the game was often slow due to the obstruction of agile defenses. This new rule will make the game more rapid.

The interruption in the circle of the free throw area will be extended into a complete circle, so that when the ball is jumped on the free throw line, the circle becomes a confining circle. In order to avoid the frequent congestion, all players except the jumpers must stand outside the circle until the ball is tapped.

This rule will make the referee's job easier. Therefore, referees will carry the ball into this area and throw it more often than before, so coaches will train fixed jump ball scoring methods in this area, which is a smart move.

The new rules also clarify the penalties for violating the center jump. Another new rule states that when a substitute reports to the referee and scorekeeper, he must provide his number, position, and the number of his opponent, if possible.

Also, there must be a fifteen-minute rest period between the two twenty-minute halves of the game, instead of ten minutes. This change will allow coaches to find ways to provide adequate skill demonstrations during the break to help entertain the audience.

Although there are many other minor changes, they will have very little impact on the training plan of coaches before the start of this season. (Note 1) (Note 3) Outline of Changes to the 1935-36 Basketball Rules

(Note 2) Situation 283 in the book "The Scenarios of the Basketball Game," published by the National Federation of State High School Associations. (The End)
