New Year's Gift Special (Next Issue)

Thoughts on Giving Gifts: Before and After 167

— Yang An

Before giving a gift, one must consider: Who is the gift for? Why give the gift? What gift to give? Where to buy the gift? How much of the gift to buy? Will the recipient find this gift useful? Will they like it? Can I afford it? These many questions swirl in the mind of the host or hostess, and it takes quite some time to decide.

The recipient of the gift is an emotional being, so one must first consider the other person's perspective. If you casually grab some useless items, shifting them from one place to another, the gift often travels from house A to B, C, D, and E, eventually returning to house A. Giving gifts is meant to build relationships, but this will only upset people. It is better not to give at all. Nowadays, everyone likes domestic goods. If I insist on giving foreign goods as gifts, I will not only be disliked but also despised. The strength of friendships lies in spirit, not in material things. If one does not consider one's financial ability and insists on showing off, giving a very expensive gift will make the recipient uneasy and suspicious. It is also useless and harmful. Psychology is recognized as a specialized field, but every class should study it. Giving gifts requires studying the recipient's psychology. It is foolish or stupid to give gifts without considering the recipient's psychology. After giving a gift, the recipient must reciprocate. There is a common saying, "It is disrespectful to refuse, but shameful to accept." Is it better to accept or decline a gift? That is the question. It is fine to accept a gift from someone close. It is reasonable to decline a gift from someone you are not close to. However, if someone sends a useless foreign product, it can be returned directly, and they can be given a lecture. If the gift-giver has another purpose or objective, it is shameful to accept and appropriate to decline. The ancients said, "A thin gift is fine for a strong friendship; true feelings do not require formalities." These are indeed profound words.

Let Me Talk About Giving Gifts 168

— Sun Choucheng

I read the previous issue of the National Goods Weekly, issue 145, from the 19th of this month, titled "New Year's Gift Special," and I am sure there will be another issue. Therefore, I will briefly state my opinions on giving gifts as follows: Mr. Yang An said, "Giving gifts is not about thickness or thinness, but about suitability; it is not about quantity, but about need." These are indeed profound words. I have always been most afraid of giving gifts. Useless items only waste money for the giver, and the recipient has no use for them. According to the principle of reciprocity, in a few days, the recipient becomes the giver and also wants to buy a gift in return. The giver becomes the recipient and also feels that it is unnecessary. Both parties suffer. Therefore, after I got married in the Republic of China era, I took my family to Jingkou three days in advance and informed my relatives and friends not to send gifts, or I would not reciprocate at all. As a result, my cousin Wang Zhefu still sent soy sauce duck and other dishes. I honestly did not stand on ceremony and did not buy a gift in return at the end of the year, which saved me a lot of trouble. In recent years, although friends in Shanghai have occasionally sent me gifts, I have never reciprocated. However, the gifts that people have sent me that I often remember and never forget include the following gentlemen: In the winter of the tenth year, when I was in mourning for my mother, Mr. Shen Jiucheng gave me a free flannel cotton robe, item 212, from the Sanyou Industrial Company. That year, because I had mourning clothes, I did not wear a silk-faced fur robe, but wore this garment through the winter. During the January 28th Incident the following year, after the 19th Route Army retreated to Kunshan, Suzhou was frequently alarmed. I detoured back to Suzhou to pick up my family. Because the Beijing-Shanghai Road was cut off early, I planned to take a boat to Jiaxing and then change to the Shanghai-Hangzhou train to Shen. The passengers were crowded. The boat was docked in the middle of the river at the Shantang Gate. I boarded the boat in the middle of the night, lost my footing, and fell into the river. Because the garment had a lot of cotton and floated, I was not in danger. Unexpectedly, it saved my life. In the winter of the year before last, Mr. Fang Jiange gave me two enamel basins with a Standing Crane brand and a pair of tea trays and two spittoons produced by the China Enamel Factory. I took them to Suzhou for home use. The colors were beautiful, the styles were ingenious, and they were durable. Every time I returned to Suzhou to wash and drink tea, seeing these items made me think of Mr. Fang's kindness. This spring, Mr. Xu Xiaochu and I were invited by Mr. Wang Xiaolai, Wang Yansong, and Pei Yunqing to tour Shaoxing. On the way back, we stayed in Hangzhou for three days. It rained every day. Mr. Xu bought a paper umbrella and gave it to me. I held this umbrella every day and enjoyed the Three Pools and Six Bridges. The interest was very strong and quite useful. During the Mid-Autumn Festival this year, my wife Sun Wuqi and I joined the Yousheng Travel Group and went to Jiaxing to visit the famous sites of Yanyu Tower, Luofan Pavilion, and Three Pagoda Temple. The weather was extremely hot in the morning, but suddenly very cold in the afternoon. The temperature difference was more than 30 degrees. I was only wearing a long Indian silk shirt, and I was very cold. Fortunately, Mr. Ren Shigang gave me a goose-brand cotton undershirt made by the Wuhe Weaving Factory, which allowed me to resist the cold and not be frozen. This fall, Mr. Yuan Hesong gave me two cans of Sanhe pickles, which I brought to my residence in Suzhou. It happened that my wife Songru was postpartum and disliked fish and meat for being greasy and did not want to eat them. She regarded this item as a treasure when she saw it, ate it greedily, and praised it endlessly. Mr. Zhou Bangjun gave me a bakelite-covered thermos and a cigarette case and a cigarette tray, all made of bakelite, the other day. I took them back to my Suzhou residence. I bring rice to school in the bottle every day, and fill it with water for washing my face. The box and tray are placed in the living room as decorations. Guests will praise their exquisite style and suitability for daily use. The items given by the gentlemen above are all domestic goods; they are not very expensive, but they are quite practical, so I have not forgotten them to this day. It can be seen that giving gifts is really not about thickness or quantity. We should pay attention to the four words "suitable and needed."

Talking about New Year's Gifts 169

— Guan Tingzhen

We humans live in society and cannot avoid contact with others. Contact leads to emotional effects, and as a result, we cannot avoid giving gifts. This is the so-called principle of reciprocity. Giving gifts can be divided into two types. One type is giving gifts among relatives. The gifts given in this type are mostly determined by customs. However, they are generally a few fixed types, so there is no need to say more. The other type is giving gifts among friends. This can be further divided into gifts for adults and gifts for children (including relatives' children). The gifts given in this type initially have no fixed restrictions, but there is a considerable range. Generally speaking, gifts for adults tend to be about food. Gifts for children? Some are edible and some are for playing. What I want to talk about here is the issue of gifts for children, with an emphasis on toys. Children are rich in imitation. No matter what others do, they will eventually learn by watching. So, how can a person grow up like this? Just look at how he learned by watching when he was young. Shouldn't we pay special attention to gifts for children? European and American countries are very concerned about gifts for children. The gifts they give mostly contain scientific meaning, such as building blocks, trains, and airplanes. There are also complete sets of small craft tools, so that children can be instilled with scientific knowledge unconsciously while playing. I remember that I once went to a park in the concession and saw several foreign children racing boats in the pool. In a corner of the park, I saw another group digging in the ground with small shovels. Several of them were busy using small lead cylinders to draw water from the pool to inject into the holes to form a fake pool. This kind of game is common for them, so it is easy to become a scientific talent when they grow up. However, the ordinary games that Chinese children play are either gambling at candy stalls or fighting with others. They rarely use scientific toys to play, so when they grow up, they only become consumers in society. Currently, China is gradually paying attention to children's scientific games, and the number of factories manufacturing such toys is also increasing. Among them, the ones that produce the most and are priced the cheapest are the Commercial Press, China Bookstore, and Kangyuan Can Factory. At the end of the year, they usually have special discounts on such toys, so that parents can buy them as gifts for children. In addition, there are many interesting books, such as children's daily newspapers, novels, and stories, which are also sold at discounted prices. They are very elegantly packaged and can also be purchased as gifts. As for sweets and other things to give to children, the Penglai Market in the South City and the National Goods Company on Nanjing Road, as well as the National Goods Market of the General Chamber of Commerce, have everything that can be purchased. If you need other special gifts that are not sold in these stores, you can directly inquire with the China National Goods Company, and they will definitely have a satisfactory answer. You must not buy foreign goods to replace them, because this is what foreigners are ashamed of.

Rational New Year's Gifts 170

— Ba Ling

Time flies like an arrow, and the sun and moon pass like a shuttle. Time passes like flowing water. In an instant, the New Year of the Republic of China, 25th year, is about to arrive again. The swiftness of time truly evokes boundless emotions in us!

As this New Year is about to arrive but hasn't yet, we open the newspapers to see that there are many advertisements, mostly displaying the eye-catching characters "New Year's Gifts." At the same time, looking at the pedestrians in the streets and alleys, many of them are carrying New Year's gifts to give to their relatives and friends. Due to this feeling, I think it is indeed a necessary thing for Mr. Yang An, the editor of the *Shen Bao* National Products Weekly, to publish a special issue on New Year's gifts today. Because the matter of gift-giving, on the surface, seems like a trivial matter, but upon closer examination, there is much room for discussion and research value, isn't there? In my opinion, a rational New Year's gift should meet the following three principles:

A. National Products: Of course! This is undeniable. When the call to promote national products is sung as high as into the clouds, we should naturally purchase national products for all our daily needs. New Year's gift-giving is a form of social interaction between people, so how can it be an exception? Therefore, our first principle in purchasing New Year's gifts is to pay attention to whether they are our country's products. For all things that are national products, even if the price is slightly more expensive, we must grit our teeth and buy them. Conversely, for all products that are not national products, even if the price is very cheap, we must not buy them just because they are inexpensive. In this severe winter, if we can take genuine national products (such as country eggs) as New Year's gifts, they will definitely be welcomed, because these things are not only authentic but also great tonics for the winter season. Furthermore, they can also provide considerable help to the lives of farmers and villagers.

B. Necessary: When giving gifts, we must not only pay attention to whether they are our country's products, but also consider the needs of the recipient. An item that someone doesn't need, even if it's given, will still be put on a high shelf, not practically used. In other words, if we can gauge the other person's psychology, observe their needs, and send practical gifts, then it will definitely make people satisfied and receive great goodwill. To put it in a scholarly way: such a gift-giving method is precisely the "doing more with less" new gift philosophy!

C. Durable: In addition to the above two principles, lastly, I think the word "durable" is also a point that we should consider when giving New Year's gifts. Because if we give gifts only for the sake of appearance and not for substance, such gifts will lose their effectiveness after a short time, which is very uneconomical. Therefore, when we give New Year's gifts, in addition to all kinds of food, cosmetics, etc., for all practical things, we must pay attention to the condition of "durability." This is also a place that cannot be ignored when purchasing New Year's gifts.

Small Experiences in Gift Giving 171

— Pu Manbin

The male head of the household is busy with matters and can't attend to trivial things. This gift-giving problem, of course, falls within the scope of the housewife's responsibilities. I'll contribute some of my small gift-giving experiences from over the years. The gifts we give can be divided into four aspects: clothing, food, daily necessities, and toys. Food and toys are certainly welcomed by children, but they should also not hinder health or damage material resources. The toys and food that I usually give people are always hygienic and meaningful. Therefore, educational toys, such as those produced by Commercial Press, China National Products Co., Kang Yuan, and other factories, I am a regular customer. Health foods from Guanshengyuan are also frequently patronized. Recently, I happened to buy cloth at Sanyou Industrial Co., and learned that their glutinous rice flour, real honey, and the well-known West Lake lotus root powder are all excellent foods, especially suitable for health in winter. I bought them and gave them to relatives and friends, who all welcomed them very much. However, for many close and thrifty relatives and friends, I also have to put some effort into clothing materials. Wang's family has a boy, so I cut two pieces of Sanyou Liberty cloth uniforms and sent them to him, and he was very happy. Li's family has two young ladies, so I bought two lengths of Gengyun brocade and Guoguang呢fabric, produced by the National Products Company Hongxin, and they were so happy that they praised them endlessly. For Mrs. Zhou, I sent two cotton wool shirts from Wuhe, and she specially called to ask me where Wuhe was located. Then, thinking about daily necessities, Mrs. Lu has many children, so I sent her a pair of Lihe basins and a kerosene stove, which she gave to her two sons who were studying in middle school. Miss Zhu is about to get married, so I chose ten items from the top-rated products of the China Chemical Industry Society, Family Industry Society, and Yonghe Industrial Co., and used them as a small token of affection. Miss Zhang Meifang and my cousin Yang Jun were engaged, so I commissioned Yaguang Bakelite Factory to make one hundred tea boxes, each with five plum blossoms inlaid on the lid, called the Five Plum Blossoms of Joy. The day before yesterday, my child came back from school and said that many classmates don't brush their teeth, so I bought a dozen Yixin toothbrushes and asked her to distribute them to her friends. I unintentionally saw that Chen Alin's socks were torn. His mother passed away early, and his father is in another province, so I bought him two pairs of Changju socks and two pairs of May 30th wool socks and gave them to this poor child. Every summer, I must go to the Wuzhou Sanfang to buy many medicines and send them to relatives and friends in the countryside as essential medicines for the family in the summer. Sister-in-law Zhu washes clothes for her eight children all day long, so I sent her two dozen Invincible soaps. She said that she usually likes to use Guben soap and Invincible soap. A certain lady, a relative of mine, developed a nervous illness. One day, I heard Mr. Qi Fanniu lecturing on Mencius and unintentionally learned that Mabin from Sanyou Society is very effective, so I bought two yuan's worth and sent it to her to try, and now she is actually cured. People say that this gift of mine is priceless. I feel that giving people national products is very valuable.

Talking About My Family's Gift-Giving 172

— Ju Ju

Time really flies like a galloping horse, and in the blink of an eye, it's New Year again. In this upcoming New Year, because of following customs, many families give each other gifts. The so-called "reciprocity..." Every year there are bound to be some gift-giving activities, but when it comes to gift-giving, it is necessary to cater to the other person's preferences. Even if it is light and insignificant, it is still a token of human affection. As the ancient saying goes, "A goose feather sent from a thousand miles away, the gift is light but the sentiment is heavy," that is a very good example.

Now let's talk about my family's gift-giving. Because my family has many relatives, most of whom live in other cities, once the end of the year and the beginning of the year arrive, some buy some gifts to visit and comfort us. But among the gifts they (or we) send, what I like best are those national product daily necessities, such as towels, bed sheets, clothing materials, etc., produced by Sanyou Industrial Co., and goose brand sanitary shirts, socks, velvet ropes, etc., from Wuhe Factory. I love to use them all, first, because they are purely national products, and we Chinese people should love Chinese goods, and second, because they are very durable. For example, the towels, Liberty cloth, printed sheets, etc., from Sanyou Society never fade in color, and the patterns are exquisite and unparalleled, and the uses are durable and long-lasting. But I have several relatives who, in order to curry favor, go to buy imported gifts to send me, but in fact, I don't welcome them. This shows their foreign-flattering mentality, but on the surface, because of human relations, I can't do anything about it. In reality, on the one hand, I politely decline, and on the other hand, I pick out a few national product gifts and send them to him (or her). This way, the gifts they send me must be national products.

When it comes to giving gifts, if there are children, it is best to place two kinds of edible gifts in the gifts. Now, the various candies of Guanshengyuan are very good—not inferior to imported goods. In the items I give away every year, I put one or two to show encouragement to the children's psychology of also using national products for food.

Then, I would like to advise the housewives of each family that when giving gifts, first, you must plan in advance what gifts each family sends, and what gifts each family wants to send. Then, you must make them more practical, mostly based on national products.

New Year's Gifts That Should Be Given 174

— Jia Guanjun

Time passes so quickly. A very thick calendar has already been torn off, leaving only a few pages. The twenty-fifth year is about to end quickly, and the twenty-fifth year is about to follow quickly. At the end of this twenty-fourth year, we must all plan New Year's gifts to give to our relatives and friends. This is a matter that cannot be avoided every year!

In the many past New Years, the gifts we gave to relatives and friends were nothing more than sweets, ham, New Year's cake, cured meat, fresh fish, colored eggs, and other kinds of food. The forms of New Year's gifts given by various places to relatives and friends may be different, but the content is always similar. I think that the gifts given for the New Year should be some daily-use gifts, because there is a lot of food during the New Year. If we give food again, it would be too much.

I will write down the New Year's gifts that should be given one by one below, which can both change the bad habits of the past and promote our country's national products.

Native cloth is the best kind of gift to give to relatives and friends in the New Year. The color is very elegant, and the material is very strong. If you make this cloth into clothes and wear them on your body, it is very simple, and it can also show that you are a person who loves to use national products. This kind of native cloth can be purchased from Sanyou Society, Hongxin Cloth Factory, Shanghai Native Cloth Company, etc. The price is not expensive, it is really cheap and good.

Overshoes are also the best kind of gift to give to relatives and friends in the New Year. They can be worn when it rains, and they can also be worn when it is sunny, which is really killing two birds with one stone. There are many factories in Shanghai that manufacture this kind of product. Among them, the cheap and good ones are of course the Double Coin brand overshoes from the Greater China Rubber Factory. They are strong and durable, and the form is beautiful. Wearing them on your feet is comfortable and beautiful.

Basins are also the best kind of gift to give to relatives and friends in the New Year, and they are also a necessary utensil for our three meals a day. There are many manufacturers of basins: such as China One, Jiuxin, Zhufeng Enamel Factory, etc. Among these three, of course, the China Enamel Factory is the best, because the enamel on the basins they make is very thick, so they are very strong. The trademark is a standing crane.

The above three kinds of goods are the best kinds of gifts to give to relatives and friends in the New Year. I hope that people from all over the world will come to buy them, which can directly save unnecessary consumption and indirectly revive our country's national products. It kills two birds with one stone, why not do it?

The China International Trade Association issued ten points of attention for national products going to the Dutch East Indies. The China International Trade Association organized an industrial inspection group to visit national product factories across the country in teams.

The National Products Movement of the Shanghai Municipal Citizens' National Products Year, which was initiated by various national product groups in Shanghai, has already organized the Shanghai Municipal Citizens' National Products Year.

The Wuzhou Guben Factory was burned down by electricity in the morning of the 21st, destroying a part of the medicine-making and small storerooms. All were insured, and the loss was still small.

The Ministry of Industry and Commerce appointed Guo Bingwen as the Director of the International Trade Bureau and Chen Feishi as the Director of the Trademark Bureau.

In order to encourage the production of national product factories, the Ministry of Railways approved the reduction of freight for the Greater China Rubber Factory, etc.

Publishing Industry

The Sorrow of the Nation 177

— Lin Yixin

Recently, due to the constant invasion of foreign enemies, the Chinese nation has suffered the most serious persecution. But this is not the real sorrow of the nation. History is full of many examples proving that a nation can struggle up under heavy pressure. The real sorrow is that at the moment when the nation's survival is in danger, there is not a single intelligent, far-sighted person to point out the path to liberation; even more sorrowful is that on the eve of the nation's collapse, it cannot arouse any reaction in a vast nation.

I remember Hegel saying the following when Germany was invaded by Napoleon in the 19th century: "Only knowledge is the only savior. Only knowledge can prevent us from being as stupidly surprised as beasts when events come, and also prevent us from using quick wits to perfunctorily deal with the present moment..." Hegel's words are truly an imperishable truth. When a nation is oppressed, if it can know how to arm itself with its own weapons, then it can still resist. The failure of resistance is a matter of the relationship between the mutual strength of facts, which can be relied upon by our efforts. The most sorrowful thing is that there is no "armament" from the beginning—in other words, there is no correct and scientific knowledge of the historical era in which a nation is located and its path to liberation. Therefore, even if one wants to revolt, there is no self-confidence whatsoever; and even if one rises up to resist, it is at most a blind action of "dealing with the moment" without conviction. Moreover, generally speaking, resistance will not exist, because it requires vast national strength. Without a certain understanding and knowledge of the overall path to liberation, national strength cannot be gathered.

China's current situation is exactly like this. I think this is his sorrow. China is now experiencing a kind of event, and the entire nation is hanging in the air. Except for listening to the natural development of the situation, no one knows where he should go. It is not useful to merely know that a certain thing or a certain force is evil, is the enemy; it is also not useful to merely know how to resist. No one knows what kind of situation the development and internal structure of the Chinese nation have reached, and how these situations have the most complex mutual relationship with external forces. But these contain important keys. Any nation is surviving, and it internally contains huge power, but these potential forces are not always able to be launched by external forces, it has its own certain laws. Only those who know this law and follow this law can move the internal strength of this nation. A nation—if not the whole, at least the most advanced part—understands this law by itself, which means the existence of the awakened spirit of this nation. If a nation can never have such an awakened national spirit, then it is equal to forever judging its fate.

Chinese history is backward, but this is not the only evidence that can be used to prove that the Chinese national spirit and general knowledge must also be equally backward. Nineteenth-century Germany was considered a backward country in Europe, but precisely because of its backwardness, this nation was actively excited in spirit. "After the fifteenth century, all the knowledge work of Western Europe was tightly condensed within the German territory for decades, as if it wanted to exhaust every ounce of strength to remedy the failure of several centuries." Therefore, the national spirit of Germany in the nineteenth century had a rich source, which was ultimately one of the major prerequisites for its strength. Similarly, twentieth-century Russia was also the most backward country in Europe, but it was able to consciously strive for its own spiritual development. Before the first revolution in Russia, Russia itself had nearly a hundred years of cultural development, overcoming the remnants of its backwardness and barbarism. This had a great relationship with the prerequisite of experience needed to create the great historical event of 1917 and its own understanding. Therefore, to repeat, we can know from this that historical backwardness cannot prove that the national spirit must also follow backwardness. On the contrary, this is precisely the place that gives us room for spiritual activity. If we know how to work hard and have worked hard, our national spirit can have a new development and can proceed at an accelerated rate; otherwise, we will have the opposite result. This is precisely determined by our subjective efforts and awareness. Therefore, within a certain limit, a nation's ability to develop its spirit is the locomotive of the nation's own ability to develop.

China is backward, but why is our national spirit so undeveloped? This is precisely the shame and sorrow of the nation itself, which cannot be attributed to history. The most sorrowful thing is that people blindly regard the general spirit of the nation as unimportant, thinking that the development of the nation can occur without the development of the national spirit. These people consider themselves "progressives." They think that the gathering of national strength can be summoned at any time like a ghost. They do not understand the great relationship between the development of the national spirit and the development of the nation itself. They do not even want to understand what the backwardness and current situation of the national spirit are. In fact, they are simply ignorant.

Not knowing the importance of the development of the national spirit means not knowing that in order to liberate the entire nation, we must first fight to remove all the shackles that restrict the free development of the national spirit. In practice, this means abandoning one's own historical task of great importance in reality.

Now, I will only say for everyone the importance and urgency of removing all the shackles on the free development of the nation.

As we said above, the development of the national spirit is the locomotive of the nation's own development. However, the development of a nation's spirit in a country does not follow a smooth path. At that time, it is often restricted in its development by old historical and social barriers. This is especially true in backward countries. If we say that the national spirit of twenty-first-century Russia has reached a high point of development, then first, it will have gone through the opportunity to strive for the free development of the national spirit. Without the opportunity for free development, the national spirit will go in the direction of suffocation, not in the direction of development.

The Chinese national spirit now has a free and possible environment for development. No. It is subject to the shackles of thought and the historical legends of society. It has the same difficulties as other nations in their historical development. Because the so-called creation and development of modern nations comes from negating their past "Middle Ages." The "Middle Ages" of each nation is the era when the nation is in a dormant state. It can be said that that era did not create the "nation" and "national spirit" in the real sense. The expression of the "Middle Ages" (in comparison with modern times) is sinking into death rather than activity, stopping rather than developing. Therefore, the universal "activity" and "development" of a modern nation are the starting point of the entire nation. In other words, in order to create and develop a nation, it is necessary to destroy things that are "medieval" and similar to "medieval" expressions. But this is a process of struggle, and it must rely on the awakened elements in the nation to call on the entire nation to go in this direction and to reject the opposite side of the nation. Because it knows that this is the condition for creating a "national spirit"—that is, the condition for "national self-gathering" and "national self-understanding." Therefore, a nation is still in a state of ignorance, and it is still unaware of striving for the development of its own spirit. That is really because in its own historical development, it has not cleared the historical path for its own development and the development of its own spirit. A nation that wants its own development and the development of its own spirit must first strive to eliminate the various conditions that hinder it. When the Chinese nation entered the modern era, it had done the work of struggling to eliminate this kind of "Middle Ages," but it did not complete it. Therefore, so far, the "Middle Ages" has become everything—or all shackles—that is pressing down on the heads of the entire nation, whether it is "restoration and reaction," whether it is the lack of freedom of speech and publication, whether it is the supremacy of thought... all are the same result. But all of these are obviously the most convenient methods for the national spirit to be paralyzed and stopped. The national spirit has entered a state of decline, and there is no more talk of "liberating itself." This is the real sorrow. I ask, under this state, what kind of serious reaction and what kind of response methods can the Chinese nation still generate in the face of the arrival of foreign enemies?

We should now often be aware that we first need a society and ideological conditions for the nation to develop freely and expand freely. Whatever contains the essence of hindering the free development and expansion of the national spirit in any environment and in any idea should be eliminated. In other words, everything that contains the essence of past "Middle Ages" legends should be eliminated. Because it violates the interests of national development, and it is simply the most unforgivable criminal of national interests. The historical task of clearing the obstacles to the free development of the national spirit is consistent with the demand for national independence. Internal national liberation and external national liberation are two sides of the same thing. We say: the social and ideological conditions that hinder the free development of the national spirit are the conditions for the death of the Chinese national spirit, and also the conditions for the death of the Chinese nation. Striving for the free and democratic development of the national spirit is the firm prerequisite for saving the nation's "national crisis."

The serious and devastated situation now is the last test of gold. All those who have thoughts and have not "died in their hearts," please consider the real "sorrow of the nation" and their own responsibilities.

Regarding the Complete Works of Gong Ding'an 178

— World Book Company

Among the famous Chinese classics published by our company is a collection of the Complete Works of Gong Ding'an. Ding'an was a great writer of the Qing Dynasty, possessing a vast and unrestrained talent. His prose was broad, profound, and remarkably modern, while his poetry was even more beautiful and elegant, imbued with a unique charm. It has been widely circulated for a long time and is a rare masterpiece in Chinese literature. Therefore, our company commissioned Mr. Wang Wenru to meticulously organize and proofread it using the methods of the imperial examination, aiming for perfection and benefiting students. Since its publication, it has been widely praised by society. Recently, we have seen two reviews of this book, one being Mr. Zhang Gongliang's review in the Book Supplement of the Ta Kung Pao, issue 102, and the other being Mr. Hong Shu's article in the Publishing World of Shen Bao (issue 31). Both gentlemen have expressed doubts and misunderstandings regarding the editor and proofreader, the elderly Mr. Wang Wenru, and therefore, our company feels compelled to make a statement.

The so-called "Hao Hao Zi" is none other than Mr. Wang Wenru's former pen name. Wang Wenru is the real name of Hao Hao Zi, which is known to all his friends. This point need not be answered by our company. However, Mr. Wang, nearing seventy years of age, passed away this autumn. The edition printed by the Chinese Studies Rotary Club was personally revised by Mr. Wang and published in the first year of Xuantong, but has long been out of print. In the winter of the 22nd year, Mr. Wang Wenru revised the old edition, adding supplements to create a complete edition, and handed it over to our company for publication. Due to our company's busy printing schedule, the manuscript was delayed for two years before finally being published this summer. This is the background of how this collection came to be. With this clarification, it should be clear that Mr. Wang Wenru would never "appropriate the work of others as his own." Our company, with its reputation for serving the cultural community for over a decade, would never deceive its readers.

We welcome and appreciate Mr. Hong Shu's enthusiastic criticism of the annotations to this collection. However, we believe that our annotations to the "Ode to Zhigui Zi" are not in error. After checking Ding'an's chronology, around the age of thirty-two, he repeatedly failed the imperial examinations. At the age of thirty-three, Mr.... studied Buddhism, with Tie Jun as his first teacher. Together with Renhe Qian Dongfu, they resided with the monk Shici Fenghua, all revering the writings of Chan Master Chewu. ... He extensively studied Tibetan, Western, Mongolian, Hui, and Manchu languages, revising the entire collection of scriptures, and consulting with experts of both old and new translations. ... Since the translation of scriptures into China, there had never been such a comprehensive effort. He also borrowed scriptures from the monk Weiyi of Longquan Temple, holding the Dharani recitation for 490,000 volumes and establishing a daily course to chant the texts of Samantabhadra and the Universal Eye Sutra. According to this, Ding'an had a deep love for Buddhism in his middle age, and the annotation stating that he "escaped to Zen due to frustration" is not inconsistent with the facts. ... In fact, the Complete Works of Ding'an has its own inherent value, and we believe that reassessing the content is more important than commenting on the annotations. But regardless, this collection remains the most complete edition of Ding'an's works available in the market, as Mr. Zhang Gongliang has acknowledged. As for any unrecorded posthumous works of Ding'an, if Mr. Hong Shu possesses such printed editions and would generously share them to benefit readers, we would be especially grateful.

Bookstore Miscellany (Continued) 179

— Li Hengzhi

The Business of Books

There are many people (especially those so-called writers who write some texts themselves) who believe that as long as the content of the book is good, people will naturally buy it. Therefore, the main problem in running a bookstore is not sales but publishing. Some who are more astute know that after a book is published, it still needs advertising and promotion. Because of this lack of understanding, many bookstores close their doors, and many writers quarrel with bookstore owners as a result.

The decisive factor for all commodities is the market, and books are no different. The commodity dumping of international capitalism requires Chinese compradors to penetrate deep into the interior; it cannot simply walk away on its own because its price is low and its quality is good. It is truly difficult for new books published by new bookstores to reach the hands of readers. Except for one or two large bookstores that have branches in various places, it is just as difficult for new books from other bookstores to invade various places for sale as it is for commodities from international capitalist countries to need a comprador; they cannot be sold without the brokers of inland booksellers. Due to the weakness of the unified market function in China, various industries still have remnants of guilds. These inland booksellers also have their own cliques. The corruption of old-style Chinese merchants is well known, and the new book industry is no exception simply because it falls within the scope of cultural undertakings.

Booksellers can also be called inland bookstores. Their origins are of two different types. One type evolved from booksellers who used to sell old books such as stone-printed "Prodigy Poems" and "Hundred Family Surnames." The other type arose with the development of the new book industry. Now, there is no difference between them. Their only business is to sell new books from new bookstores in Shanghai and other ports to their locations. Their scale varies. Some are very large, such as the Pei Wen Zhai and Yu Yu Wen in North China, which even have their own branches and well-organized sales networks. However, most are small in scale. Their only business method is to connect with local schools to promote their sales—of course, this is only the case for a few. Most only have a storefront, do some advertising, and entice readers to buy on their own. But even so, they have a significant impact on the new book industry. Without them, your new book would not be able to reach their location, and you would lose that market. Naturally, this is also due to the generally low level of education in China. Otherwise, readers who need books could simply order by mail, without the need for their intermediaries at all. But in reality, most Chinese readers of new books cannot pay attention to the publication of the books they need at any time. The sale of general books is nothing more than: "Oh, is there such a book? I'll buy one." If a book cannot be placed in front of the reader, there will be no sales.

Thus, managers and salesmen of new bookstores in Shanghai must win over those inland booksellers. However, the inland booksellers treat the book business no differently than they treat the business of foreign cloth and sundries; they simply sell books as one of the commodities. They have no opinions on culture, academics, or even the content of the books—they simply don't understand. What they value most is: First, will this book sell? Second, what is the price and discount of this book, and is it profitable for us? Third, is there any political problem with this book, that is, will the Public Security Bureau seal their doors for selling this book? (In the past, there were too many such incidents). Their profits depend entirely on the large-scale sale of books. This inevitably leads them to favor a few large bookstores. Therefore, their main business relies on books from a few large bookstores. For newly opened small bookstores, because they do not know which books are stable and can be sold in large quantities, they generally do not want to distribute them. As a result, there are often such interesting things happening:

"No, this kind of book doesn't sell. It's too much trouble to keep accounts!" The inland bookseller said to the manager of the newly opened bookstore, even though those books are the most valuable and the most likely to sell.

"Friend, please help me out. I'm just asking you to take it and try to sell it. You can have it as a gift. You don't have to send it back if you can't sell it." The shrewd manager begged like this. After the bookseller took the books to the interior and sold them all, and the readers flocked to buy them, the bookseller, driven by profit, would inevitably ask the new bookstore to replenish the stock. At that time, the new bookstore manager's plan would succeed, either by asking the bookseller for payment or even by not sending the books if the payment did not come.

If a small new bookstore wants to develop its sales network, it must win over inland booksellers. But inland booksellers, because of the location of the source of their goods, in turn flatter those large new bookstores. Their most important method is to secure special agency rights. The so-called "special agency" means exclusive sales within a certain area. Everywhere we see, in addition to "exclusive sales office of a certain bookstore in a certain place," there are also "branch of a certain bookstore in a certain place." These so-called branches are mostly unrelated to the main store; they are just special sales agents. New bookstores can use the relationship of special sales to accept a certain amount of deposit, and also stipulate that the special sales office must achieve a certain amount of business each year. If the books published by that bookstore sell well, then the sales agent will naturally obey the bookstore. Otherwise, if the new books are stopped from being sent, the sales agent will have to close their doors. Therefore, the larger the scale of the new bookstore, the easier it is to collect debts. Some say that in today's new bookstore business, where most people suffer bad debts or cannot collect debts, the accounts of the Commercial Press's sales offices will not go unpaid. This is why.

In order to expand the sales network, new bookstores make great efforts to win over inland booksellers and small bookstores. Large bookstores are even more favored. Inland booksellers, whether they are owners or managers, mostly come to Shanghai once every festival or every year to settle accounts and order goods. The organization of the Chinese New Book Industry Association may not have much important function, but there is a kind of natural unity on Fourth Horse Road in Shanghai. Whenever an inland bookseller arrives in Shanghai, managers and salesmen of various bookstores who have some affection for each other will pass the word around, as if a living god of wealth has arrived. They will treat them to dinner, win them over, and do their best. If the bookseller brings some cash to pay the bill or order goods, then the inn where he stays will be as bustling as a marketplace. Colleagues often have disagreements over this. Which bookstore's bill has been paid, which bookstore's goods have been allocated less, everyone will compete.

The old-style Chinese commercial dealings are built on so-called "friendship." "I have a friendship with you, you have to pay me more money, and add more goods for me." The methods of creating "friendship" are wine, opium, mahjong, watching plays, and so on. It was like this before, and it is still mostly like this now. Although we dare not say that all the business of the new book industry is like this, no one can deny that this set of things still exists. Therefore, there are often booksellers who come to Shanghai to settle accounts and end up with syphilis all over their bodies, unable to return home. This is of course mostly due to their own weak will, but it cannot be said that it is not related to that kind of improper social intercourse. Some say that the decline of Chinese commerce is due to the poor transaction system. If we borrow this saying to apply to the new book industry, then the way the new book industry does "business" really needs to be improved. (To be continued)

Recently, the price of Xiang lotus seeds has risen sharply due to the lack of inventory in the Hankou market. According to reports, the remaining 120 boxes of Wuxi lotus seeds were snapped up by various merchants at 40.4 yuan each. Even if some goods arrive en route, they will definitely be hoarded. Telegrams from Changde also reported a rise of 3 to 4 yuan, and further tightening is expected.

Oil Market: Chen Hong Tung Oil Sells Out and Prices Soar 183

Since the price of white tung oil soared, the cost of Hongjiang tung oil has increased exponentially. New oil has not yet arrived. It is reported that various oil mills in the production area calculate the cost per barrel to be above 30 yuan, even for the secondary brand. However, the consumption of domestic products is not as high as one-tenth or two-tenths of the export trade. Moreover, after the bankruptcy of rural areas, the purchasing power of farmers is weak. If the price is too high, it will hinder sales. Even with the secondary Hongjiang oil priced at 30 yuan per barrel, it is already a rare sight in the domestic sales market. However, it is still insufficient in terms of cost. Therefore, it can be asserted that the sales market for new oil in the future will definitely be less than in previous years. All the old oil in this port is about to be sold out. Only one or two out of ten companies have a slight inventory. The price of Zhen Hong Jichanghe has been sold to 37.6 yuan per barrel. Fu Hong Yang Hengyuan has already sold out. Qing Yuanfeng is selling at over 30 yuan. Buyers must pay 31 yuan to purchase. It is the highest price since the market began.

White Tung Oil with Fluctuating Prices 184

The recent situation of white tung oil has been erratic, with prices rising and falling constantly. However, the selling price in the Hankou market has always been around 50 yuan per dan. The highest price last week soared to 52.8 yuan, but this week it has fallen back to 50 yuan. The attitude of foreign firms is that around 50 yuan is still a reasonable price. If it is as high as 55 or 56 yuan, then they may or may not buy. At 50 yuan to enter customs, all foreign firms want to purchase. Therefore, whenever the price in the Hankou market falls to 47 or 48 yuan, foreign firms will definitely rush to purchase. As a result, there is no hope for overly cheap prices. Moreover, in recent months, it has become the number one export commodity in our country, and those engaged in this business have paid very close attention. The future situation will generally be around 50 yuan as the lowest limit. Foreign firms in this port also have occasional small transactions, but one or twenty tons are not enough to move people's hearts. It is not as good as the hundreds of tons in the Hankou market, which can influence the market.

Riding breeches are used in large quantities for tailoring, and the selling price has risen again. Kongshi brand is even more popular. Yesterday, each yard was sold at a uniform price of 8.25 yuan. Metals: Sichuan Sales of New Galvanized Wire Are Very Brisk 189

Yesterday was the anniversary of the Yunnan Uprising, and also Christmas, so all agencies, foreign firms, and major commercial firms were closed for one day. The metal trade was also very sparse. Moreover, with the continuous rain, there were even fewer visitors to the market. Among the goods on offer, except for the frenzied purchase of new galvanized wire by Sichuan merchants, there were very few transactions for other goods. The market was calm, with no major changes. It is said that new galvanized wire such as Nos. 8, 10, 12, and 16 to 25 were all on offer. It is reported that the total number of transactions reached as many as 2,450 bundles. The most number of offers came from metal firms along North Suzhou Road. The merchants who bought the most were Yuhecheng, Xie Kang, and Chuan Han Cheng. In addition, the Sichuan Commercial Company of Wanxian also bought quite a lot. In short, since the purchase of new galvanized wire, the amount of goods in the market has felt reduced. If there are not many arrivals within the year, then the future market trend may be upward.

Yarn and Cotton: Major Changes in the Yarn and Cotton Market in the Past Week Various Market Prices Exceeding the Highest Peaks Many Brokers Reorganized A Glimpse of the Recent Bull and Bear Front 190

In the past week, the yarn and cotton market suddenly showed a lively trend. Overseas silver shrank sharply, and the gold standard rose from around 1,150 yuan to 1,200 yuan, reaching the peak since the reform of the legal tender. Market rumors spread like wildfire, saying that customs gold units were about to rise sharply. Speculators were actively involved, and financial circles, securities firms, gold traders, and public debt merchants all focused on the yarn and cotton market. The momentum was extremely fierce, and the market gradually soared. The low price of May futures was 201.5 yuan before December 17th, but reached a peak of 211.8 yuan on the 23rd, rising by 10.3 yuan. Later, because the sales of spot yarn were not very brisk, and the end of the year was approaching, the demand from all parties shrank. Manufacturers began to sell, and at the same time, the gold standard turned from a peak to a decline. A wave of enthusiasm was temporarily dispersed. However, the overseas calculated prices for American cotton rose by 1.3 yuan, while Indian cotton only rose by 0.6 yuan. The current cotton market is sluggish due to factory demand, and export trade has stalled. Japanese merchants are also hesitant to purchase. Therefore, it is difficult to revive market prices. However, the low price of May futures for gold standard cotton was 43.22 yuan on the 16th, and rose to 45.85 yuan on the 23rd, which shows the general craze for speculation. Recently, the chips of both bulls and bears have been increasing day by day. Once there is a change, the range of ups and downs becomes larger and larger. It is not surprising that each market rises or falls by 2-3 yuan. In fact, with this group of new troops, there will inevitably be many events in the future. If the environment is slightly favorable, the momentum will come like swarming bees, and it is extremely difficult to resist the sharp momentum. The future changes are difficult to predict. The situation of brokerages in the exchange changing hands is even more developed. No. 1 has been renamed Deda, No. 70 has been changed to Jinkang, No. 37 has been changed to Changxing, No. 38 has been changed to Huamao, and No. 63 has been changed to Jinghua, and they have all started business on the market. It is said that most of the capital is added by public debt, gold, and banking circles. Therefore, the transfer fee for brokerage licenses has improved compared to before. The recent yarn lineup shows that those buying are Tongji, Dafu, Jinchang, Gengfeng, Yuanyi, Changfeng, and Jinkang, ranging from 4,700 bales to 13,100 bales. The majority of the buyers are in the banking, gold, and public debt sectors. Those selling are Yudada, Dafeng, Daji, Hexing, Tongfeng, Shenji, Yichang, and Ruida, ranging from 7,000 bales to 10,000 bales. Fellow traders, some merchants, Japanese merchants are the center. The buyers of gold standard cotton are Tongji with 64,700 dan, Changhe with 59,100 dan, and Gengfeng with 23,500 dan as giants. The sellers are Shenchang with 38,800 dan, Shenji with 35,300 dan, Yuanxingchang with 44,500 dan, Kehe with 23,000 dan, and Yikang with 21,600 dan. Statistics: The Impact of the Implementation of Legal Tender in Shanghai During the First Month (Continued from Previous Issue) - All Indices Rise Sharply 193

Retail Price Index: The general index is 103.3, an increase of 9.8% compared to 94.1 last month, and an increase of 5.1% compared to 98.3 in the same month last year. This is the highest index since August 1933. Among all items, 123 items increased, 9 items decreased, and 22 items remained unchanged. In terms of the extent of the increase, 2 items increased by 50% to 60%, 2 items increased by 40% to 50%, 7 items increased by 30% to 40%, 16 items increased by 20% to 30%, 42 items increased by 10% to 20%, and 54 items increased by less than 10%. Compared with last month, all types of indices have increased. The metal category increased by 14.0%. Due to the lack of spot goods, the prices of copper ingots and large lead bars have risen sharply, increasing by 43% and 32% respectively. Black iron pipes increased by 23%, and small tin ingots increased by 17%. Other items such as round steel and tinplate have also increased. Building materials increased by 12.6%. Except for cement, all items increased. Fir and paint oil increased by 33% and 25% respectively. Textiles increased by 12.3%. Due to the soaring price of raw silk and the depletion of spot goods, the price per dan (unit of weight) has increased from 93 yuan last month to 145 yuan this month, an increase of 5%.

6. Over twenty silk factories in this city have suspended operations due to the shortage of raw silk for various types of silk. Production has decreased and market prices have soared. Last month, the price per dan of Huangchang silk was 520 yuan, Ji Li Gan silk was 450 yuan, and Bai Chang silk was 710 yuan. This month, Huangchang silk has risen to 780 yuan, Ji Li Gan silk to 660 yuan, and Bai Chang silk to 970 yuan. Huangchang silk increased by 50%, Ji Li Gan silk by 47%, and Bai Chang silk by 37%. Silk, crepe, rayon, silk floss, yarn, cotton cloth, woolen cloth, and velvet have also increased. Fuel increased by 10.5%, with kerosene rising particularly sharply. The market price per case has increased from 7.45 yuan last month to 9.45 yuan this month, an increase of 27%. The increase rate of the other four types of indices does not exceed 10%, and the smallest also reaches 5.6%.

Export Price Index: The general index is 89.6, an increase of 11.2% compared to 80.6 last month, and an increase of 24.4% compared to 72.0 in the same month last year. This index has been extremely low in recent years. This month's index is the highest since September 1932. Among all items, 55 items increased, 5 items decreased, and 6 items remained unchanged. Compared with last month, all three types of indices have increased sharply. Raw materials increased by 12.9%. Most items have risen sharply, especially dried silk floss, rapeseed, red sorghum, factory silk waste, soybeans, sesame, and bulk coal, with increases ranging from 20% to 56%. Manufactured goods increased by 10.4%. Except for tung oil, which saw a sharp drop of 25% due to the new goods entering the market, most goods have increased, especially various types of raw silk, raw oil, and soybean oil. Consumer goods increased by 7.6%. Prices of silk, crepe, egg yolk, eggs, green tea, coarse cloth, firewood, and charcoal have all risen sharply.

Import Price Index: The general index is 141., an increase of 15.4% compared to 123.7 last month, and an increase of 5.9% compared to 134.8 in the same month last year. This month's index is the highest record since November 1931. Among all items, 69 items increased, 1 item decreased, and 12 items remained unchanged. Compared with last month, all three types of indices have increased sharply. Raw materials increased by 21.1%. Items that have risen sharply include copper ingots, fir, large lead bars, American cotton, and tin solder, with increases ranging from 20% to 43%. Consumer goods increased by 14.1%, such as kerosene, white sugar, Florida oranges, White Tower oil, and black pepper, with increases ranging from 20% to 27%. Manufactured goods increased by 11.9%. Market prices of items such as white wood yarn increased by 32%, glossy paper and Daolin paper increased by 30%, kraft paper increased by 29%, rayon, black iron pipes, and diesel increased by 23%, motor oil increased by 22%, and angle iron increased by 21%. The increase rate for most items ranges from 10% to 20%.

Cost of Living Index: The general index is 109.2, an increase of 5.1% compared to 103.9 last month, and an increase of 0.4% compared to 108.8 in the same month last year. Among all items, 30 items increased, 3 items decreased, and 10 items remained unchanged. The reason for the increase is partly due to the impact of retail prices, and partly due to the sharp depreciation of copper coins. The average exchange rate on the 1st and 15th of last month was 342 coins, but the average this month has shrunk to 318 coins, which means that retail prices quoted in copper coins have increased by about 7% when converted to national currency. Except for rent, all five types of indices have increased compared with last month. Fuel increased by 10.5% due to the increase in kerosene, firewood, and matches. Clothing increased by 6.7%, with various types of cotton cloth increasing. Miscellaneous items increased by 5.1%, including cigarettes, soap, toothpaste, etc., which are all priced in copper coins in the market. Food increased by 4.6%. Although soybean oil, soybeans, flour, and white sugar have increased sharply, spinach, green vegetables, and radishes have plummeted due to seasonal factors and abundant production. Therefore, the increase in this category of index is relatively moderate. (To be continued)

Empty Positions Covered When American Cotton Closed

Yesterday, when the American cotton market opened, the situation was stagnant, with a decline of 2 to 6 points in each month. The market focused on the December term. Before the cessation of the December term, only two delivery notices were issued, the last bull position in the December term was liquidated, and the January term was greatly affected. However, other months were still relatively firm, and dealers were still buying. Empty positions shifted to October, and there were few transactions, showing signs of the upcoming holiday. When closing, empty positions were covered, and the market rose again. The spot price fell by 5 points, and futures prices, except for the first month (January) which fell by 3 points, rose by 2 to 4 points for the remaining months. The spot price of English cotton fell by 5 points, and the futures price fell by 3 points. Bull positions in Indian cotton were liquidated, and European exporters sold off. There were few buyers, and the market was weak. The prices of Pingguo cotton fell by 1.25 to 1.5 rupees, and the prices of Oumula and Bairoxi cotton fell by 2.5 rupees. Shen Bao Local Supplement

Commentary

Our Country's Foreign Policy 194

— Li Min

New Foreign Minister Zhang Qun stated his foreign policy to journalists on the 18th, saying that China's foreign policy is to seek the adjustment of international relations with sincerity and integrity, and to abolish unequal obligations through legal channels. This is the foreign policy of our government. The Japanese government should be very satisfied with this, and there is no suspicion that our country has any [anti-foreign] sentiments.

Since the [September 18th Incident], Japan has often accused our government of not having full [sincerity] in accepting the [friendship] and [cooperation] policies it proposed. This is the Japanese government blaming us for lacking integrity in international relations. But with our people's ignorant thinking, we can always figure out that the so-called sincerity and integrity should first be based on mutual benefit and equality. While Japan is occupying a large amount of our country's territory by force and continues to attack the interior of China, it blames our country for lacking integrity in international relations. It is really impossible to know where integrity can be established? Unless China completely becomes India or Korea, and before the Chinese people are completely bombed by Japanese planes and bombs, we really cannot find where this international integrity under command can be established.

Sun Yat-sen, in his Three Principles of the People, explained with the utmost seriousness that the first way for China to seek independence and liberation is to abolish the various unequal treaties imposed on us by foreign countries. What are these unequal treaties? "They are the deeds of sale of the entire Chinese nation]!" This is the most brilliant sentence that Mr. Sun Yat-sen ever said. At the moment of Mr. Sun Yat-sen's death, in his last and most important will—the will that everyone respectfully reads today—he earnestly instructed his descendants: "[Recently advocated convening a national assembly. And abolishing unequal treaties, it is especially necessary to promote their realization in the shortest possible time." Where did the various unequal treaties imposed on China come from? This was created by the force of artillery and airplanes. Japan graciously tells us: If China wants to abolish unequal treaties, it should do so after [establishing its own national system and improving the modern national structure] (see the Japanese Associated Press telegram on the 19th). We really cannot know how China, with more than 3.8 million square miles of territory, can establish its own national system while it is directly occupied by force, and how more than 1.2 million square miles of territory (Hebei and Chahar provinces) can improve its modern national structure under the control of foreign forces, with the possibility of being directly occupied immediately? Unequal treaties are fundamentally illegal things. It is somewhat vague to ask imperialism to automatically withdraw from the territory it occupies in our country through peaceful negotiations, unless the earth can turn over.

In fact, to establish China's own national system and improve the modern national structure is not impossible. As the saying goes: "An eye for an eye, a tooth for a tooth," this is the only way for China to establish its own national system and improve the modern national structure.

Goddess 195

"Ah, ah! How hateful, how hateful! How hateful that I have been utterly defeated! I wish I could cut off that cunning Zhuanxu's head and use it as my drinking vessel!" At that time, Gonggong had already fled to the broken part of Buzhou Mountain. His legs were so sore that he could not support himself, and he was so thirsty that he sat down and licked the blood on his knife. His partisans were scattered at the foot of Buzhou Mountain. (15)

Fist 196

— Wen

Ahu had a pair of fists, iron fists. Relying on this pair of fists, he stood astride both banks of the Yellow River, and his fists hit north, south, east and west. He dominated this street.

Ahu had no home. During the day, he waited in the teahouse for the sun to set, and at night he nested in the gambling house. But he didn't gamble for money. The gambling house boss provided him with food and bedding just because he had a pair of fists. Ahu sat in the gambling house, and the gamblers did not dare to owe debts or fight. Ahu patted his chest with complacency: "Bah, my fists!"

In the eyes of respectable people, Ahu was a thorough rascal. He walked swaying and filled the entire street. A cheap felt hat was perched on his back. He never wore long clothes all year round. The buttons on his short clothes were densely arranged like ribs. Around his waist was a silk belt embroidered with two dragons snatching a pearl. His face was covered with bulging muscles, and half a cigarette butt was stuck to the corner of his mouth. Even before you saw him, you could hear a series of "Damn your mother!" But when he stepped onto the street, he was the boss. No one dared to call him Ahu to his face. He had a ledger with him. He used circles and lines to record the names and amounts of each debtor. He came out of the gambling house and collected money from the street stalls. For example, if you borrowed one yuan, you would pay back ten cents of silver every day for ten days. If you borrowed ten yuan, you would pay back one yuan every day. The stallholders would never be able to pay off his debts. If the old debts were not cleared, he could lend you money again to repay the debts. The circles and lines on the ledger would never be erased. However, Ahu had a pair of iron fists, and his fists created his position.

With his pockets full of silver dollars and coins, Ahu went to the teahouse. The teahouse owner always greeted him with a smiling face: "Good business?"

Ahu shook his head. He didn't understand business. "I have capital to lend, so I'm not afraid they'll be short a penny!" As he said this, he threw the money from his pocket onto the table. He stretched his legs and firmly propped his back against the wall, calculating according to the marks on the ledger. At the place where a bearded old man was drawn, Ahu opened his mouth with triangular eyes.

"Boss, where does that damned son of Qian Laotou live? Damn it! He hasn't come to the street to do business for three days. Humph, does he want to赖债(lai zhai)?" See my fists!" With a bang, he slammed the table, causing it to yell.

The teahouse owner smiled at him. Ahu's pair of lawless fists had lost their effect on Qian Laotou. The boss slowly walked over, imitating Ahu's strength, and patted him on the shoulder:

"Boss, are you looking for Qian Laotou? You'll have to wear iron shoes to collect this陰債(yin zhai)!"

"What?" The boss shouted: "Did this old man die three days ago?"

Ahu opened the ledger, cursing "Damn it!" in his mouth, calculating those horizontal and vertical marks: "Humph, it's twenty-five yuan! Since he hasn't paid interest for three days, add three yuan, three corners, and two cents. Boss, does he have anyone else at home? If he doesn't pay me back, watch my fists!" Another bang.

"He has a sixteen-year-old daughter," a gambler in the gambling house抢着(qiang zhe) said: "Isn't it worth it to buy a wife for twenty-eight yuan?"

Ahu smiled. For many years, he had only been obsessed with money. He had never thought about getting a woman. This was an opportunity to get a wife to play with. Ahu thought, grabbed his pocket, and rushed down the teahouse.

That night, Ahu didn't return to the gambling house. The gamblers talked, saying that he had gone to find Qian Laotou's daughter. One gambler even joked:

"Does anyone want to borrow money? Go to Miss Qian, and don't be afraid of his fists."

Ahu didn't go to the street the next day. People with good intentions went to Qian Laotou's house. The door of Qian Laotou's house was敞着(chang zhe), and there was no one there. Ahu was lying in Miss Qian's bed, with blood flowing on the bed. Ahu's pair of iron fists were chopped off, his eyes rolled back, and he was断气了(duan qi le).

The local保(bao) secretly reported to the police station, raised money for a pine coffin to bury him, and no one dared to bring up this matter.

Song Introduction 197

The Uncrowned Emperor

Why do you sometimes cry, baby? Why do you sometimes smile, little one? Are you feeling empty and hungry, that's why you're crying and wailing like that? Are you feeling full, that's why you're smiling like that? Are you tired? Then close your eyes tightly and sleep soundly. Are you awake? Open your eyes and reach out for Mommy and big sister to hold you. Can you walk now? Then be energetic all day and run and jump around. You eat well, sleep well, and always smile sweetly. Your eyes are bright and you can see everything, dear! Your ears are sharp and you can hear everything, dear! Your tiny nose has a sensitive sense of smell, and your tiny tongue has a sensitive sense of taste. Your small heart is clear, and your small brain is as quiet as a mountain. Your pure and authentic soul is sparkling, and everyone cherishes you. I cherish you, I like you, you have firmly grasped the hearts of all people. You are truly an uncrowned emperor, and everyone supports you. You love your father, love your mother, and love all people under heaven!

Sinology 198

Feng Mingquan's Ancient Prose Masterpieces

Li Shude (940) 7:30 AM to 8:30 AM

Topic: Spring in Tang's Random Notes (3)

When people have happy events, they use opera performances to celebrate. Often the performance of actors with court robes continues until the end of the celebration. This is a performance celebrating the birthday of Guo Fenyang. My wife, Yao Furen, asked me, "The court robes fill the courtyard, it can be said to be grand. What will happen after this?" I said, "You must have something to say. Please tell me." Madame said, "Please allow me to recite a poem. 'The old mountains and rivers in front of the gate have not changed. The broken captives once served under Ma Fubo. In the future, I will pass through the place of singing and dancing alone. The ancient locust trees are sparse and the setting sun is plentiful.' This is Zhao Gu's poem passing through the old residence of Fenyang. 'The old residence of Fenyang is now a temple. Only the singing and dancing tower remains from that time. Forty years have passed, the carriages and horses have dispersed. The ancient locust trees are deep in the alleys, and the evening cicadas are sorrowful.' This is Zhang Ji's poem about the East Tower of Faxiong Temple. If you want to know what happened after the actors with court robes have finished, please recite these two poems." I was saddened. Now that my wife has passed away, I recall this and write it down.

Xing Ruiting Hairpin Phoenix

Huiling (1380) 9:00 PM to 10:00 PM

Opening: "The Widow"

The cold moon shines brightly through the gauze window. A woman with a wretched fate guards a cold room. Without rouge and powder, her face is pale. Facing the mirror, she sighs with tears in her eyes. Dressed in plain white, her moth-like eyebrows are lowered. Silently, she thinks secretly. Remembering how happy she was when she married her beloved. They flew together like loving mandarin ducks. His love was like lacquer, deeply fond of her. Her affection was like glue, tied to her beloved. She really hoped to live a long life with him in harmony. With inseparable mandarin ducks singing in harmony forever. Who knew. The river of love is vast and full of storms. Taking her beloved's life. I, the widow, originally intended to follow him to the underworld. But I have elders in the family hall. I can only, endure the lingering grief and steal a remnant of life. Endure tears and secretly hurt myself. Evening and morning, I frequently worship before his spirit tablet. Tears flow like ropes as I offer pepper sauce. His remaining appearance is vivid as I look with concentration. No wonder he always smiles at me. I look at myself. He thinks of himself. How can I get him to comfort my heart with gentle and warm words? He must know that I have wasted my youth and my appearance is haggard. Like a flower without a master, blooming in vain. Sleeping in a cold quilt is like iron. The simple curtain is a lonely phoenix after his death. The sad years are like bitter weeds. The splendor has all turned into a yellow dream. To whom can I tell my grievances? I store ten thousand kinds of regrets in my heart. How pitiful, her delicate cries are like flowing water. Startling the cold crows to fly far away. The parrot does not know human hatred. In front of the curtain, it still imitates the sound of crying. She cried until her voice was hoarse, her tears were exhausted, and she had no strength. Only then did she wipe both eyes with silk. Panting, she stood up and leaned on the dressing table. Lazily, she slowly stepped onto the bed. How pitiful, her soul communicates faintly in the underworld. She meets her lover in the land of Hua胥. When she wakes up, it's still just a dream.

Movie News

Love Song Not a Sentimental Intention on the Screen 203

"Love Song Not a Sentimental Intention". It is a play within a play in Yang Cun's new work "Spring Flower". The protagonists are Gao Zhanfei and Zhu Qiuhen. Although this is a short episode. Readers can easily imagine its story from these words. It is very interesting. Moreover, the dialogue is especially easy and humorous, making people can't help but laugh—Director Wu Cun's style is inherently known for its delicate and appropriate style. This time in "Spring Flower" there are many unexpected gimmicks. The various aspects of the film industry are all captured on camera.

Mr. Wang Goes to the Countryside's Sound and Light 204

"Mr. Wang Goes to the Countryside", directed by Tang Jie, every shot is repeatedly studied before shooting begins, even for one shot, Tang Jie. Ye Qianzi, Zuo Ming, Cao Xuesong and others argued for a while before resolving it.

"Mr. Wang Goes to the Countryside", the shadow is arranged by Yan Bingchong, and the angle and light of each shot are painstakingly considered. The clarity of light is rarely seen in recent domestic films. All the scenery is exceptionally beautiful, like a refined and unparalleled picture.

"Mr. Wang Goes to the Countryside", the sound is recorded by He Zhaohuang, Zhaozhang, and Maogang. In addition to clear dialogue, all rural birdsong, chicken crows, frog croaks, and cow calls are all vividly and realistically reproduced.

Yuan Meiyun Sings Mountain Songs 205

Sweet Scenes in "Triumphant Song"

In the lotus pond, in the gentle breeze, Yuan Meiyun and her younger brother Liu Li are rowing a small boat there to pick water chestnuts. In the blue sky, the singing of the old women in the distance is heard from afar, and Meiyun finally could not help but sing lightly leaning on the side of the boat. The lyrics are:

The weather in Jiangnan in June is fine,

Sisters are picking red water chestnuts in the pool,

The sharp water chestnuts prick your hands,

The scorching sun scorches people.

Oh my God! God,

There is no rain during the plum rain season,

There is no 18-year-old girl who does not marry,

Thinking of youth in the water chestnut mirror.

Wang Guilin of the Yi Hua sound film "Triumphant Song", which will be released soon, said to everyone: "We don't rely on heaven, we don't ask God!"

When Meiyun sang to here very sweetly and at the same time very sadly, Liu Li smiled and shamed her and said, "Sister, aren't you afraid of being embarrassed?" And just as Meiyun was about to raise her hand to hit Liu Li, a burst of laughter suddenly flew from the shore. Meiyun raised her head and took a look. I couldn't help but blush and feel extremely ashamed.

This is a beautiful scene in the upcoming Yi Hua sound film, a huge production directed by Bu Wancang, "Triumphant Song". The clear and melodious singing makes people intoxicated and forget all the worries in the world.

Tragedy Under Drought Qin Tong Beaten by Thugs 206

A village near Zhoujiaba suddenly had a brutal beating case. The famous old star Qin Tong was beaten and injured. The details are recorded as follows:

Since spring, there has been no rain in Jiangnan, the dead grass covers the wilderness, and the mournful swans soar in the sky. The phenomenon of drought has already appeared. Farmers in various villages regard water as life, and bloody cases often occur due to the struggle for a little river water.

A farmer named Qin Tong in a village in Zhoujiaba is over sixty years old. He only has a young grandson and granddaughter under his knees. Under this scorching sun, he has no choice but to work hard to draw water, but because he is old and weak, he is of no use. On the other hand, the neighboring fields have sufficient water due to machine pumping. He couldn't help but feel jealous, so he tied the embankment to divert the water from the neighboring fields into his own, but in the end, he couldn't bear his conscience and filled the breach again. However, the matter was discovered, and he was beaten and injured. Qin, as an old man, could not withstand the destruction of violence. His head was already broken and bleeding, and he was dying!

How will this bloody case be resolved? Will Qin Tong be saved? Please watch the upcoming Yi Hua sound dialogue giant film, "Triumphant Song" directed by Bu Wancang tell you.
